The Second Proof: Universal Human Practice
Al-Razi argues from universal human practice of blessing or cursing the dead.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Razi's proof from universal human practice for the soul's survival after death and how it relies on innate disposition.

Core Idea
The universal practice of blessing or cursing the dead testifies to the soul's survival.

Al-Razi presents his second proof, drawing on a fact observable across all times and cultures: humans universally bless the good dead and curse the evil dead. If the soul perished with the body, this practice would be meaningless. But the entire human race cannot unanimously engage in a vain practice; it must be rooted in an innate truth. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once through, then read the literal translation. Notice Al-Razi's style: he builds his argument step by step.
The passage is compact; each sentence carries logical weight.
2
Identify the observation and the conditional
Al-Razi begins by observing a universal practice: people invoke mercy for the good dead and curse for the evil dead. He then poses a conditional: if the person does not survive death, this practice would be vain.
The conditional is the key move: it sets up the absurdity.
3
Understand the argument from impossibility of universal falsehood
Al-Razi argues that it is impossible for all people across all times to be engaged in a vain and false practice. Since the practice is universal, it must reflect a genuine reality.
This is a consensus argument, but grounded in innate disposition (fitra).
4
Formulate the conclusion
The only way to avoid the absurdity is that the soul survives death and is distinct from the body. The practice presupposes a living subject after death.
The conclusion is that the human being (self) is other than the body.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية : وهي قريبة مما تقدم . إنا نرى جميع طوائف العالم ، وجميع الفرق متفقين على أنه إذا مات إنسان. فإن اعتقدوا فيه أنه كان حال الحياة ، موصوفاً بالصفات المحمودة : ذكروه بالرحمة والتعظيم ، فتارة يقولون : صلوات الله عليه . وتارة يقولون : رحمة الله عليه . وإن اعتقدوا فيه أنه كان حال الحياة موصوفا بالصفات المذمومة من الجهل والشرور والإيذاء : ذكروه باللعن والخزي والعذاب. ولو قدرنا أن الإنسان لم يبق حياً بعد موت البدن ، لكان هذا الكلام عبثاً باطلا ، فإن من لا يكون حياً ، استحال اتصال الرحمة والروح والراحة إليه ، واستحال أيضاً إيصال الذم واللعن إليه . ولو كان الأمر كذلك ، لكان أهل المشرق والمغرب من الزمان الأقدم إلى هذا الزمان مطبقين على الفعل الباطل والقول الفاسد ، وهذا بعيد . فإن إطباق الخلق العظيم على العلم الباطل غير ممكن. فهذا يدل على أن فطر النفوس وبدائه العقول شاهدة بأن الإنسان شيء آخر غير هذا البدن ، وأنه يبقى بعد موته حياً ، فإن كان سعيداً كان أهلاً للرحمة ، وإن كان شقياً كان أهلاً للعنة
The second proof: It is close to what preceded. We see that all sects of the world, all groups, agree that when a person dies, if they believe that during life he was described with praiseworthy attributes, they mention him with mercy and veneration, sometimes saying 'Blessings of God be upon him' and sometimes 'Mercy of God be upon him.' And if they believe that during life he was described with blameworthy attributes of ignorance, evils, and harm, they mention him with curse, disgrace, and punishment. If we supposed that the person does not remain alive after the death of the body, this speech would be vain and false. For whoever is not alive, it is impossible for mercy, spirit, and comfort to reach him, and it is also impossible to direct blame and curse to him. And if it were so, then the people of the East and West from the earliest time to this time would be unanimously engaged in vain action and corrupt speech, and that is far-fetched. For the agreement of a great creation upon false knowledge is not possible. This indicates that the innate dispositions of souls and the primary intuitions of intellects bear witness that the human being is something other than this body, and that he remains alive after his death; if he is felicitous, he is deserving of mercy, and if he is wretched, he is deserving of curse.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage presents the second proof for the survival of the soul. Al-Razi argues from universal human practice: all people, regardless of time or place, when they believe a deceased person was good, they invoke mercy upon him, and when they believe he was bad, they invoke curse upon him. If the person were not alive after death, such invocations would be meaningless, as mercy and curse can only affect a living being. Since the entire human race has consistently done this across history, their consensus on this practice cannot be based on falsehood; it must reflect an innate truth. Thus, the natural disposition of souls and the primary principles of reason testify that the human being is something other than this body and that he remains alive after death, deserving of reward or punishment.

Key Terms
الحجة
البدن
النفس
الرحمة
اللعن
فطر النفوس
بدائه العقول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The practice of blessing or cursing the dead is merely a social custom or convention with no deeper truth.
Correction: Al-Razi argues that the universality and consistency of this practice across all cultures and times indicates it is rooted in an innate disposition (fitra), not mere custom. If it were false, it would not be universally maintained.

Checkpoint
According to the second proof, why would invoking mercy or curse on the dead be meaningless if the soul did not survive?
A) Because the dead cannot hear us.
B) Because mercy and curse can only reach a living being.
C) Because it is a waste of time.
D) Because people only do it out of habit.

Key Takeaway
The universal human practice of invoking mercy or curse on the dead is evidence that the soul survives death and is distinct from the body.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you speak well of a deceased person, do you genuinely believe your words reach them, or do you view it as mere custom? What does your answer reveal about your conviction in the soul's survival?
?
If Al-Razi is correct that all of humanity's practice is rooted in an innate truth, why do you sometimes act as if death is the end? Where in your life do you need to align your actions with the reality of the soul's continuation?
?
The dead are either deserving of mercy or curse based on their deeds. Knowing that your own soul will survive, what is one habit or intention you must change today to ensure you are among those deserving mercy?

The Third Proof: Grave Visits and Seeking Help
Al-Razi presents the grave visit evidence for the soul's survival.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the widespread practice of visiting graves and experiencing benefit from the dead serves as evidence for the survival of the soul.

Core Idea
If the dead were truly gone, seeking their help would be meaningless.

Al-Razi presents the third proof by observing a common human practice: visiting blessed graves, praying, fasting, and supplicating there, and finding tangible results. He argues that such practices would be absurd if the soul of the deceased had perished. This lesson examines that argument and its logical foundation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on grave visits
Read the first part of the Arabic passage up to the conclusion about nullity if souls were not remaining. Then read the translation.
Notice the mention of Aristotle's students as a supporting anecdote.
2
Understand the logical structure
Al-Razi presents a conditional: if souls did not survive, then seeking help from a dead person (who lacks sensation) would be futile. Since we observe benefit, the consequent is false, so the antecedent is false.
This is a modus tollens argument.
3
Assess the strength of the evidence
Consider whether the observed benefits are genuine or could have alternative explanations (e.g., psychological suggestion). Al-Razi treats them as empirical evidence.
This connects to the common misunderstanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثالثة : إنه جرت عادة العقلاء بأنهم يذهبون إلى المزارات المتبركة ويصلون ويصومون عندها ، ويدعون الله في بعض المهمات ، فيجدون آثار النفع ظاهرة ، ونتائج القبول لائحة . يحكى أن أصحاب أرسطاطاليس ، كانوا كلما صعبت عليهم مسألة ، ذهبوا إلى قبره ، وبحثوا فيها ، فكانت تنكشف لهم تلك المسألة ، وقد يتفق أمثال هذا كثيراً ، عند قبور الأكابر من العلماء والزهاد في زماننا ولولا أن تلك النفوس باقية بعد موت الأبدان ، وإلا لكانت تلك الاستعانة بالميت الخالي عن الحس والشعور عبثا وذلك باطل . ومما يقوي هذا : هو أن الأحياء قد يصلون لأجل الأموات ، وقد يتصدقون لأجلهم . وقد يتفق كثيراً : أن الحي إذا نام عند قبر بعض الأموات ، فإنه يراه في المنام ، وقد يدله على أمر مخصوص ، وقد يدله على دفين ، كان هذا الحي غافلا عنه ، وقد ينبهه على بعض المهمات . وكل ذلك يدل على أن النفوس باقية بعد موت الأجساد ، وكل ما دل على أن النفس باقية بعد موت الجسد ، فإنه يكون دليلا على أن النفس غير الجسد
The third proof: It is the custom of rational people that they go to blessed shrines, pray and fast at them, and supplicate God in some important matters, and they find manifest effects of benefit and clear results of acceptance. It is narrated that the students of Aristotle, whenever a problem became difficult for them, they went to his grave and investigated it, and that problem would be revealed to them. Many similar occurrences happen at the graves of great scholars and ascetics in our time. Were it not that those souls remain after the death of bodies, then that seeking help from the dead who lacks sensation and consciousness would be vain, and that is false. What strengthens this is that the living may pray for the sake of the dead, and may give charity for their sake. And it often happens that when a living person sleeps at the grave of some dead person, he sees him in a dream, and he may guide him to a specific matter, or guide him to a buried treasure that the living person was unaware of, or alert him to some important matters. And all of this indicates that the souls remain after the death of bodies, and everything that indicates that the soul remains after the death of the body is evidence that the soul is not the body.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage presents the third proof for the survival of the soul. Al-Razi adduces empirical observations: rational people visit blessed graves, pray and fast there, and experience tangible benefits. He cites the anecdote of Aristotle's students who, when stuck on a problem, would go to his grave and find the solution revealed to them. Such occurrences, he argues, would be meaningless if the dead person's soul had perished, because asking help from a mere corpse is futile. Additionally, he notes that the living pray and give charity for the dead, and often see the dead in dreams, receiving guidance. All these phenomena indicate that souls survive the body. Moreover, since these phenomena are only intelligible if the soul is distinct from the body, they also prove that the soul is a separate substance from the body.

Key Terms
المزارات المتبركة
الاستعانة بالميت
النفوس
الأبدان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that visiting graves and praying there is merely a psychological comfort with no real effect from the deceased.
Correction: Al-Razi argues that if the dead had no awareness, then such acts would be futile. But since benefits are observed, it indicates the soul is aware and capable of intercession.

Checkpoint
What is the logical structure of Al-Razi's argument from grave visits?
A) If souls remain, then seeking help is beneficial.
B) If seeking help is beneficial, then souls remain.
C) If souls do not remain, then seeking help is futile. Since seeking help is not futile, souls remain.
D) If seeking help is futile, then souls do not remain.

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi uses the widespread practice of seeking help at graves and experiencing benefit as empirical evidence that the soul survives the body.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever visited a grave and felt a sense of connection or help? Did you truly believe the deceased was aware, or was it just a cultural practice? How does Al-Razi's proof challenge you to examine the sincerity of your belief in the soul's survival?
?
If you were faced with a difficult problem, would you consider seeking help from a deceased righteous person? What does your answer reveal about your conviction that the dead are alive in another realm?
?
When you pray near a grave, do you expect something to happen? Are you willing to accept that such practices are evidence that the soul continues, or do you dismiss them as superstition? What would it mean for your daily life if you truly believed the dead can hear you?

The Third Proof: Dreams of the Dead
Al-Razi presents the dream evidence for the soul's survival.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how dreams in which the dead provide guidance serve as evidence for the soul's survival and its independence from the body.

Core Idea
Dreams of the dead giving real guidance prove the soul's continued existence.

Al-Razi strengthens his third proof with another common experience: the living dream of the dead, who may provide them with information, such as the location of a hidden treasure or advice on important matters. He argues that such occurrences cannot be explained if the soul has perished, and they further indicate that the soul is distinct from the body.

Guided Path
1
Read the dream argument
Read the second part of the passage, from 'وما يقوي هذا' to the end, and its translation.
Notice that Al-Razi includes praying and giving charity for the dead as related evidence.
2
Analyze the dream phenomenon
Al-Razi describes cases where a living person sleeps at a grave and sees the dead in a dream, receiving guidance about a hidden treasure or important matter.
3
Connect to the conclusion
Al-Razi concludes that all such phenomena show the soul remains after death, and since they involve interaction, the soul must be a separate substance from the body.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And all of this indicates that the souls remain after the death of bodies, and everything that indicates that the soul remains after the death of the body is evidence that the soul is not the body.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you dream of a deceased loved one, do you dismiss it as random brain activity, or do you consider that their soul might actually be present and may have a message for you? How would your life change if you began to treat such dreams as real guidance from the unseen?
?
If the souls of the dead can still interact with the living and reveal hidden truths, what does that mean for your relationship with those who have passed away? Is there something they would want you to know or do that you have been neglecting? Will you take time to reflect on this and act accordingly?
?
Al-Razi uses even seemingly mundane dreams as proof that you are not merely a body. In your daily choices, do you live as though you are destined for eternal existence, or do you act as if this life is all there is? What is one concrete change you can make today to prioritize your soul over your body?

The Fourth Proof: The Soul's Return in the Quran
Al-Razi cites Quran 89:27-30 as proof of the soul's survival after death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Razi uses Quran 89:27-30 to argue that the soul survives death and returns to God.

Core Idea
The soul's survival after death is directly attested by the Quran's command to return to God.

Al-Razi continues his series of proofs for the soul's immortality, now turning to scripture. He cites a powerful verse where God addresses the tranquil soul directly. This passage unpacks the verse to show that the soul's essence persists after the body dies, returning to its Lord in a state of felicity.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and its context
Read the Arabic of Quran 89:27-30 and its translation. Notice that God speaks directly to the soul, commanding it to return.
The verse is from Surah al-Fajr, often recited at funerals.
2
Understand Al-Razi's identification of the soul
Al-Razi identifies the 'tranquil soul' as the accountable person who has turned away from corporeal things toward spiritual realities. This soul is the true self.
3
Examine the three attributes of the soul at return
The verse describes the soul with three attributes: tranquil in true knowledge and ethics, pleased with God, and pleasing to God. Note that these attributes survive the body's death.
These attributes show the soul's perfection and readiness for paradise.
4
Grasp the conclusion that the soul remains alive after death
Al-Razi concludes that the entire passage is a clear statement that the real human essence remains alive, intelligent, and understanding after the body's death.
This directly supports the doctrine of the soul's immortality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الرابعة : الآيات الدالة على أن الإنسان بعد موته يرجع إلى الله في السعادة والكرامة . قال تعالى : ( يا أيتها النفس المطمئنة ، ارجعي إلى ربك راضية مرضية فادخلي في عبادي وادخلي جنتي ) ولا شك أن المراد من هذه النفس المطمئنة : هو ذلك المكلف الذي حصل له اطمئنان ، بأنه يجب الإعراض عن الجسمانيات، والإقبال على عالم المفارقات والروحانيات . ثم إنه تعالى قال لهذه النفس : ارجعي إلى ربك راضية مرضية ) وهذا الرجوع لا يحصل إلا بعد الموت ، ثم إنه تعالى وصفها حال الرجوع بهذه الصفات الثلاثة : أولها : كونها مطمئنة في العلوم الحقة ، والأخلاق الفاضلة ، التي لا تزول بسبب زوال الجسد . ثانياً : كونها راضية عن خالقها في جميع الأحوال . وثالثها : كونها مرضية عند الله تعالى في جميع الاعتقادات والأخلاق . ثم لما وصفها الله تعالى بهذه الصفات قال لها : ( فادخلي في عبادي ، وادخلي جنتي ) وكل ذلك تصريح بأن الشيء الذي هو الإنسان في الحقيقة باقي ، حي ، عاقل فاهم بعد موت هذا البدن
The fourth proof: The verses indicating that the human being after his death returns to God in felicity and honor. He, exalted, said: 'O tranquil soul, return to your Lord, well-pleased and well-pleasing, and enter among My servants, and enter My Paradise.' (89:27-30) There is no doubt that the intended meaning of 'the tranquil soul' is that accountable person who has attained tranquility, that it is necessary to turn away from corporeal things and to turn towards the world of separate substances and spiritual things. Then He, exalted, said to this soul: 'Return to your Lord, well-pleased and well-pleasing' and this return does not occur except after death. Then He, exalted, described it at the time of return with these three attributes: First: its being tranquil in true sciences and virtuous ethics that do not disappear due to the disappearance of the body. Second: its being pleased with its Creator in all circumstances. Third: its being well-pleasing to God, exalted, in all beliefs and ethics. Then when God, exalted, described it with these attributes, He said to it: 'Enter among My servants, and enter My Paradise.' And all of that is a clear statement that the thing which is the human being in reality remains alive, intelligent, understanding after the death of this body.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth proof, drawn from the Quran. Al-Razi cites the verse in which God addresses the 'tranquil soul' (al-nafs al-mutma'innah) and commands it to return to its Lord. He explains that this soul refers to the accountable person who has achieved tranquility by turning away from physical concerns and toward spiritual realities. The command 'return' indicates that this return occurs only after death. Then God describes the soul at the time of return with three attributes: tranquility in true knowledge and virtuous character that do not perish with the body, being pleased with God, and being pleasing to God. After these descriptions, God commands entry into Paradise. Al-Razi concludes that this whole passage is a clear declaration that the real essence of the human being—the soul—remains alive, intelligent, and understanding after the death of the body.

Key Terms
النفس المطمئنة
ارجعي إلى ربك
الرجوع
الجسمانيات
المفارقات
الروحانيات
الصفات الثلاثة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse refers only to a physical resurrection at the end of time, not an immediate return after death.
Correction: Al-Razi emphasizes that the command 'return' occurs after death, pointing to an immediate post-mortem existence of the soul.

Checkpoint
According to Al-Razi's interpretation, what does the command 'return to your Lord' imply about the soul?
A) The soul returns to the body after death.
B) The soul returns to God after death.
C) The soul returns to the grave.
D) The soul returns to this world.

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi demonstrates that the Quranic address to the tranquil soul proves the soul's conscious survival after death and its return to God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the verse 'O tranquil soul, return to your Lord,' do you feel it is a future promise or a present command for you to start turning away from worldly attachments right now? What specific attachment is the hardest for you to release?
?
Al-Razi says the soul must be 'well-pleased with God in all circumstances.' Is there a circumstance in your life right now where you are not pleased with God's decree? How can you work toward that attribute before death?
?
If you died tonight, would your soul be described as 'tranquil in true knowledge and virtuous ethics'? What is one truth you need to embrace or one virtue you need to practice starting today to become that soul?

The Verse of the Tranquil Soul and Its Three Attributes
Razi introduces the fourth proof with the verse of the tranquil soul and explains its three attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi uses the Quranic verse of the tranquil soul to identify three attributes that characterize the soul at the moment of its return to God, establishing its spiritual nature.

Core Idea
The soul's three attributes prove it is a spiritual entity addressed after death.

Razi presents his fourth proof for the soul's survival by directly engaging with a Quranic verse that addresses the soul. By analyzing the verse, he extracts three attributes—tranquility, being pleased, and being pleasing—that describe the soul at the time of its return to its Lord. This lesson focuses on that verse and those attributes, which form the foundation of the proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and its explanation
Read the Arabic verse 'يا أيتها النفس المطمئنة...' and its translation. Notice that the verse is addressed directly to the soul, not the body.
The verse is from Surah al-Fajr (89:27-30).
2
Identify the three attributes
From Razi's commentary, list the three attributes: tranquility (اطمئنان), being pleased (راضية), and being pleasing (مرضية). Understand each one.
These attributes are described as lasting even after the body's disappearance.
3
Reflect on the implication
Ask yourself: why does describing the soul with these attributes after death support its survival? Consider that the soul is being addressed and characterized independently of the body.
This connects to the broader argument that the soul continues to exist.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الرابعة : الآيات الدالة على أن الإنسان بعد موته يرجع إلى الله في السعادة والكرامة . قال تعالى : ( يا أيتها النفس المطمئنة ، ارجعي إلى ربك راضية مرضية فادخلي في عبادي وادخلي جنتي (۱) ) ولا شك أن المراد من هذه النفس المطمئنة ) : هو ذلك المكلف الذي حصل له اطمئنان ، بأنه يجب الإعراض عن الجسمانيات، والإقبال على عالم المفارقات والروحانيات . ثم إنه تعالى قال لهذه النفس : ارجعي إلى ربك راضية مرضية ) وهذا الرجوع لا يحصل إلا بعد الموت ، ثم إنه تعالى وصفها حال الرجوع بهذه الصفات الثلاثة : أولها : كونها مطمئنة في العلوم الحقة ، والأخلاق الفاضلة ، التي لا تزول بسبب زوال الجسد . ثانياً : كونها راضية عن خالقها في جميع الأحوال . وثالثها : كونها مرضية عند الله تعالى في جميع الاعتقادات والأخلاق . ثم لما وصفها الله تعالى بهذه الصفات قال لها : ( فادخلي في عبادي ، وادخلي ) وكل ذلك تصريح بأن الشيء الذي هو الإنسان في الحقيقة باقي ، حي ، عاقل فاهم بعد موت هذا البدن [ وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول : الإنسان باقي ، (۱) الفجر ۲۷ - ۳۰ والتكملة من ( ل ، ط ) . وإلى ربك فيها تأويلان : ١ - إلى جسد صاحب النفس - وهذا يدل على أن النفس غير الجد . ٢ - إلى ربك أي إلى الله تعالى ـ وهذا يدل على أن النفس هي الروح والجسد . وهو صحيح . والرجوع إلى الله في الآخرة، أي ارجعي إلى ثراب ربك وكرامته . وادخلي في عبادي أي في الصالحين منهم ، وادخلي الجنة معهم . حي ، عاقل ، فاهم بعد موت هذا البدن . والبدن (۱) ] ليس كذلك . وهذا يدل على أن الإنسان شيء مغاير لمجموع هذا البدن ، ولكل واحد من أجزائه وأقسامه . ويقرب من هذه الآية قوله تعالى : ( حتى إذا جاء أحدكم الموت ، توفته رسلنا . وهم لا يفرطون . ثم ردوا إلى الله. مولاهم الحق . ألا له الحكم وهو أسرع الحاكمين (۲) ) فحكم عليهم بعد موتهم : بأنهم ( ردوا إلى الله . مولاهم الحق) وذلك يقتضي بقاؤهم بعد موت البدن ، وعلى أنه تعالى يحاسبهم بعد موت البدن . وكل ذلك يدل على ما ذكرناه . فإن قالوا : فلم لا يجوز أن يكون المراد بهذا الخطاب : جزء [ مخصوص ] من أجزاء البدن ؟ فنقول : فعلى هذا التقدير يكون المكلف المشاب والمعاقب والمخاطب والمعاتب ، ليس إلا ذلك الجزء ، فيكون الإنسان هو ذلك الجزء ، لا هذا البدن . ولا شيئاً من الأعضاء المحسوسة كالقلب والدماغ . ونحن لا نطلب إلا هذا القدر في هذا المقام.
The fourth proof: the verses indicating that after his death, man returns to God in happiness and honor. He said the Most High: (O tranquil soul, return to your Lord, well-pleased and pleasing, and enter among My servants and enter My Paradise (1)). There is no doubt that what is meant by 'the tranquil soul' is that responsible person who has attained tranquility, namely that it is necessary to turn away from corporeal things and turn towards the world of separate entities and spiritual things. Then the Most High said to this soul: 'Return to your Lord, well-pleased and pleasing' (and this return occurs only after death). Then the Most High described it at the time of return with these three attributes: First: its being tranquil in true sciences and virtuous morals that do not disappear due to the disappearance of the body. Second: its being pleased with its Creator in all circumstances. Third: its being pleasing to God in all beliefs and morals. Then when God described it with these attributes, He said to it: 'Enter among My servants and enter.' All of that is a declaration that the thing that is man in reality is remaining, living, rational, understanding after the death of this body [and if this is established, we say: man is remaining, (1) Al-Fajr 27-30 and the completion from (L, T). And 'to your Lord' has two interpretations: 1 - to the body of the owner of the soul - this indicates that the soul is other than the body. 2 - to your Lord meaning to God Almighty - this indicates that the soul is the spirit and the body. And it is correct. And the return to God in the afterlife, i.e., return to the dust of your Lord and His honor. And 'enter among My servants' i.e., among the righteous of them, and enter Paradise with them. living, rational, understanding after the death of this body. And the body (1) is not like that. And this indicates that man is something different from the totality of this body and from each of its parts and divisions. And close to this verse is His saying the Most High: (Until when death comes to one of you, Our messengers take him, and they do not fail. Then they are returned to God, their true Lord. Unquestionably, His is the judgment, and He is the swiftest of reckoners) (2). So He judged them after their death that they are 'returned to God, their true Lord,' and that necessitates their remaining after the death of the body, and that He will hold them accountable after the death of the body. All of that indicates what we have mentioned. If they say: Why is it not permissible that what is meant by this address is a specific part of the body? We say: On this assumption, the responsible agent who is commended, punished, addressed, and rebuked is only that part, so man is that part, not this body, nor any of the sensory organs like the heart and brain. And we seek nothing more than this in this context.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth proof for the survival of the soul after death, based on the Quranic verse of the tranquil soul (النفس المطمئنة). The author classifies the three attributes of the soul at the moment of return to God: tranquility in true knowledge and virtues, being pleased with the Creator, and being pleasing to God. The argument is that the soul is addressed after death, indicating its independent existence. The author then anticipates an objection suggesting the address might refer to a specific bodily part, and responds that if so, that part would be the true human, not the entire body, which still supports the soul's survival. The proof is reinforced by another verse from Surah al-An'am about the angels taking the soul at death and returning it to God for judgment.

الاطمئنان
الرجوع
راضية
مرضية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the address to the soul is metaphorical or refers to the body's state.
Correction: Razi takes the address literally: the soul is a distinct entity that is tranquil, pleased, and pleasing, and these attributes persist after death.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic address to the tranquil soul with three enduring attributes establishes the soul as a spiritual entity that survives bodily death.

The Argument from Post-Death Address and the Objection
Razi argues that the post-death address proves the soul's survival, answers an objection, and cites a supporting verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the fact that the soul is addressed after death proves its survival, and how Razi refutes the objection that the address might refer to a bodily part.

Core Idea
The soul's post-death address proves its distinct existence from the body.

After presenting the verse and its attributes, Razi draws a logical conclusion: the very fact that the soul is addressed after death demonstrates that it continues to exist independently. He also anticipates an objection that the address could be to a specific part of the body, and responds by showing that even then, that part would be the real human. This lesson unpacks that argument and the supporting verse from Surah al-An'am.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument from the passage
Read from 'وكل ذلك تصريح' to the end of the passage. Notice how Razi concludes that man remains after death because he is addressed.
The key phrase is 'وكل ذلك تصريح بأن الشيء الذي هو الإنسان في الحقيقة باقي'.
2
Identify the objection and response
Look for the objection starting with 'فإن قالوا' and Razi's response. Understand the logic: if the address is to a part, that part is the true self.
This response shows that even the objection supports the soul's distinction from the body.
3
Consider the supporting verse
Read the supporting verse from Surah al-An'am about angels taking the soul at death and returning it to God. See how it reinforces the argument.
This verse is cited as additional evidence for survival after death.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the address 'O tranquil soul' refers to the person's body or a bodily part that disintegrates.
Correction: Razi argues that the address is to a non-bodily entity because the attributes described (tranquility, pleasure, etc.) are not properties of the body, and even if it were a bodily part, that part would be the true self.

The Fifth Proof: The Soul as Another Creation
Razi uses the sixth stage to argue the soul is a different creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Qur'anic phrase 'another creation' proves that the human soul is not a physical substance but a distinct creation from the body.

Core Idea
The soul's creation is 'other' – not a body transformation but a separate realm.

In this lesson, we examine a key Quranic argument for the immaterial nature of the soul. Imam al-Razi presents the fifth proof based on Surah al-Mu'minun, where God describes the stages of human creation. The sixth stage, the attachment of the spirit to the body, is uniquely called 'another creation,' signaling that the spirit belongs to a different order of existence. Let's explore the logical force of this distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic passage
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation carefully. Notice the contrast between the first five stages and the sixth.
The verse is from Surah al-Mu'minun (23:12-14).
2
Identify the six stages
The first five stages are bodily changes from clay to a formed embryo. The sixth stage is the attachment of the spirit. Observe how the Qur'an describes the sixth stage with the special phrase 'then We produced him as another creation.'
This phrase is not used for any of the previous stages.
3
Understand the argument
The author argues: if the spirit were physical, it would be just another bodily change and the Qur'an would have used the same language. But it uses 'another creation,' indicating the spirit is from a different realm, not the world of bodies. Consider the implication for the soul's nature.
The proof is linguistic: the change in wording signals a change in substance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الخامسة : قوله تعالى : ( ولقد خلقنا الإنسان من سلالة من طين (٥) ) فذكر المراتب الخمسة في التغيرات الجسمانية . ثم قال في المرتبة السادسة منها ، وهي مرتبة تعلق الروح بالبدن : ( ثم أنشأناه خلقاً آخر ) وهذا يدل على أن الروح ليس من عالم الأجسام ، وإلا لكان ذلك أيضاً تغيراً للجسم من حالة إلى حالة أخرى ، فكان من جنس المراتب الخمسة المتقدمة . وكما لم يقل في شيء منها : ( ثم أنشأناه خلقاً آخر ) وجب أن لا يذكر هذا (1) من (م) ، ط ) . والإنشاء الآخر . قال فيه القرطبي : قيل هو نفخ الروح فيه بعد أن كان جمادا . وعن ابن عباس : خروجه إلى الدنيا . وعن مجاهد : كمال شبابه . والصحيح : أنه عام .
The fifth proof: His saying the Most High: (And indeed We created man from an extract of clay (5)) and He mentioned the five stages in bodily changes. Then He said in the sixth stage among them, which is the stage of the attachment of the spirit to the body: (Then We produced him as another creation). And this indicates that the spirit is not from the world of bodies, for otherwise that would also be a change of the body from one state to another, and it would be of the same kind as the five preceding stages. And just as He did not say in any of them: (Then We produced him as another creation), it is necessary that He did not mention this (1) from (M, T). And 'the other creation' - al-Qurtubi said about it: It is said it is the blowing of the spirit into him after he was inanimate. And from Ibn Abbas: his emergence into the world. And from Mujahid: his full youth. And the correct view is that it is general.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth proof for the distinction between the spirit (روح) and the body, based on the Quranic verse from Surah al-Mu'minun. The author notes that God describes five stages of bodily development from clay, but then the sixth stage is described as 'another creation' (خلقاً آخر). This indicates that the spirit is not a mere physical transformation like the previous stages; otherwise it would have been grouped with them. The author argues that the use of the phrase 'another creation' shows that the spirit is from a different realm, not from the world of bodies. The footnote then provides various interpretations of 'another creation' from classical commentators, but the author seems to affirm the general meaning that it refers to the spirit.

Key Terms
الروح
خلقاً آخر
المراتب الخمسة
تعلق الروح بالبدن
عالم الأجسام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All six stages of creation are purely physical transformations.
Correction: The Qur'an distinguishes the sixth stage as 'another creation,' proving the spirit is not a physical change like the previous stages.

Checkpoint

A) That the spirit is made of a finer substance
B) That the spirit is not from the world of bodies
C) That the spirit is created after the body
D) That the spirit is eternal

Key Takeaway
The Qur'an's use of 'another creation' for the soul's stage proves the soul is non-physical and from a different realm.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Objection: The Self as a Specific Body Part?
The author rebuts the objection that 'man' refers to a specific part of the body.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses an objection to clarify that the true self is not the body but the specific part that is addressed and held responsible.

Core Idea
If only a part of the body is addressed, then the self is that part alone.

The author anticipates a possible objection to his argument that the human being is something other than the composite body. The objector suggests that the scriptural address might refer only to a specific part of the body. The author's response is both clever and concise: even if that were the case, the self would still be that part, not the whole body. This lesson walks through the logic of that response.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Understand what the opponent is suggesting – that the scriptural address might be directed to a specific part of the body, not the whole.
The objector is trying to undermine the author's claim that the human being is distinct from the body.
2
Identify the author's reply
Notice how the author accepts the assumption for argument's sake and then draws the logical conclusion.
The author says 'on this assumption' to show that the objection does not harm his position.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
The author says that on this assumption, the responsible self is only that part, so the human being is that part, not the body or its organs.
This means the self is still something other than the composite body.
4
Ask: why does this matter?
This shows that even if the opponent's objection is granted, it still supports the author's overall thesis.
The objection actually reinforces the idea that the human being is not the physical body.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا : فلم لا يجوز أن يكون المراد بهذا الخطاب : جزء [ مخصوص ] من أجزاء البدن ؟ فنقول : فعلى هذا التقدير يكون المكلف المشاب والمعاقب والمخاطب والمعاتب ، ليس إلا ذلك الجزء ، فيكون الإنسان هو ذلك الجزء ، لا هذا البدن . ولا شيئاً من الأعضاء المحسوسة كالقلب والدماغ . ونحن لا نطلب إلا هذا القدر في هذا المقام
If they say: Why is it not permissible that what is meant by this address is a [specific] part of the parts of the body? We say: On this assumption, the responsible one who is rewarded and punished and addressed and rebuked is only that part, so the human being is that part, not this body, nor any of the sensible organs like the heart and the brain. And we seek nothing more than this extent in this place.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer pair. The objector suggests that the scriptural address might refer only to a specific part of the body, not the whole body. The author replies that even if that is the case, then the human being (the true self) is that part, which is distinct from the rest of the body and from the visible organs. Thus, the objection still supports the author's thesis that the human being is something other than the composite body. The author concludes that this much is sufficient for his purpose.

Key Terms
مكلف
مخاطب
جزء مخصوص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that if the Quranic address is directed to a specific body part (e.g., the heart or brain), then the human being is that part without any distinction from the rest of the body.
Correction: The author shows that even if the address is to a specific part, that part becomes the true self, distinct from the body and its other organs, thus reinforcing that the self is not the composite body.

Key Takeaway
The author shows that even if the scriptural address refers to a specific body part, that part is the real self, distinct from the body, supporting the thesis that the human being is not the composite body.

The Soul as a New Creation
Author argues from Quran 23:12-14 that the soul is not from the world of bodies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quranic verse about the soul's creation as 'another creation' proves that the soul is not from the world of bodies.

Core Idea
The soul is a new kind of creation, not just another bodily stage.

This lesson examines the fifth scriptural proof from Al-Matalib al-Aliyah, which uses Quran 23:12-14 to argue that the soul belongs to a realm beyond the physical. The author compares the six stages of human creation and highlights the unique phrase 'then We produced it as another creation' to show that the soul is not merely a bodily transformation. Let's unpack the reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its literal English translation. Let the author's words speak first before analyzing.
Pay attention to the flow from the five bodily stages to the sixth.
2
Identify the five bodily stages and the sixth
The verse mentions five stages of bodily changes (nutfah, 'alaqah, etc.) and then a sixth stage where the soul attaches. Notice that only the sixth stage is described as 'another creation'.
The author assumes the reader knows the five stages from the Quranic context.
3
Understand the logical argument
The author argues: if the soul were just another bodily change, God would not have used a distinct phrase. Since He did, the soul must be of a different nature.
This is an argument from divine speech patterns.
4
Grasp the linguistic clue
The phrase 'then We produced it as another creation' (ثم أنشأناه خلقاً آخر) is unique to this stage. It signals a qualitative shift, not just a quantitative change.
The word 'آخر' (another) indicates a different kind, not more of the same.
5
Conclude with the doctrinal point
The soul is not from the world of bodies (عالم الأجسام). It is a distinct, non-material creation from God.
This aligns with the broader Islamic belief in the soul's immortality and separate existence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الخامسة : قوله تعالى : ( ولقد خلقنا الإنسان من سلالة من طين ) فذكر المراتب الخمسة في التغيرات الجسمانية . ثم قال في المرتبة السادسة منها ، وهي مرتبة تعلق الروح بالبدن : ( ثم أنشأناه خلقاً آخر ) وهذا يدل على أن الروح ليس من عالم الأجسام ، وإلا لكان ذلك أيضاً تغيراً للجسم من حالة إلى حالة أخرى ، فكان من جنس المراتب الخمسة المتقدمة . وكما لم يقل في شيء منها : ( ثم أنشأناه خلقاً آخر ) : وجب أن لا يذكر هذا اللفظ في هذه المرتبة أيضاً . وحيث خص هذه المرتبة بهذا اللفظ ، دل ذلك على أن الروح ليس من جنس الأجسام .
The fifth proof: His statement, exalted be He: 'And indeed We created man from an extract of clay' — He mentioned the five stages of bodily changes. Then He said in the sixth stage among them, which is the stage of the soul's attachment to the body: 'Then We produced it as another creation.' And this indicates that the soul is not from the world of bodies; otherwise that would also be a change of the body from one state to another state, and would be of the same kind as the previous five stages. And just as He did not say in any of them: 'Then We produced it as another creation,' it was necessary that He not mention this expression in this stage either. And since He singled out this stage with this expression, that indicates that the soul is not of the same kind as bodies.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth scriptural proof for the soul's non-bodily nature. The author cites Quran 23:12-14, which describes the creation of man from clay through several bodily transformations (nutfah, 'alaqah, mudghah, etc.), and then a sixth stage where God says 'then We produced it as another creation.' The author argues that this new creation (al-khalq al-akhar) cannot be merely another bodily change, because that would be similar to the earlier five stages. Since God explicitly distinguishes this stage with a special phrase, it shows that the soul belongs to a different order, not the world of bodies (not min jins al-ajsam).

Key Terms
سلالة
طين
أنشأناه خلقاً آخر
عالم الأجسام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The soul is just a subtle or refined body (latif jism) and thus part of the physical world.
Correction: The Quranic phrase 'another creation' indicates that the soul is not from the world of bodies (laysa min 'alam al-ajsam), meaning it is an entirely different kind of creation, not a subtle body.

Checkpoint

A) Because it involves a material change
B) Because God uses the special expression 'then We produced it as another creation'
C) Because the soul is material
D) Because it is similar to the previous stages

Key Takeaway
The Quranic phrase 'another creation' in the sixth stage of human creation proves that the soul is not from the world of bodies.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your soul is a direct act of God's creation, distinct from any bodily process, does your daily life reflect that you value your soul more than your body? Think about one habit that nourishes your soul and one that only gratifies your body. Which receives more of your time?

The Quran says the soul is 'another creation'—something entirely new, not a product of physical evolution. What would change if you truly believed you were created from a different world?
?
The author argues that consistency in divine speech demands a difference in kind. Is your life consistent with the belief that your soul is not reducible to biology? Examine your priorities: are you more concerned with the health of your body or the state of your soul before God? What step can you take today to treat your soul as the 'other creation' it is?

The Soul Hovering Over the Bier: Proof of Immortality
Two hadiths proving the soul's survival and its distinction from the body.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses two prophetic hadiths to prove that the soul is the true human self that survives bodily death.

Core Idea
The soul's speech over the bier proves the human being is the soul, not the corpse.

This lesson presents the sixth proof from the author, based on two prophetic traditions. The first hadith describes the soul of the deceased hovering over the bier and addressing the family, showing that the soul remains conscious and active. The second hadith from the Battle of Badr reinforces this, as the Prophet addressed the dead and they heard him. Together, these texts demonstrate that the soul is the real self that continues after death, distinct from the body.

Guided Path
1
Read the two hadiths carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the vivid description of the soul fluttering and speaking, and the Prophet's address to the dead at Badr.
These are textual proofs (samiyyat) from prophetic reports.
2
Analyze the first hadith's argument
The author argues that the soul's speech—addressing the family as 'my family'—identifies the soul as the true person. Since the soul persists, the human being persists even after the body dies.
3
Consider the second hadith's support
The Prophet's address to the dead polytheists at Badr indicates they hear and understand, even though their bodies are dead. This shows the living self (al-hayy) is different from the dead body.
This reinforces the first proof.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Both hadiths lead to the conclusion that the human being is not the material body but an immaterial soul that survives death. This is a core doctrine in many Islamic theological schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السادسة : قوله عليه السلام في بعض خطبه : « إذا حمل الميت على نعشه رفرفت روحه فوق النعش ، وتقول : يا أهلي ويا ولدي . لا تلعبن بكم الدنيا ، كما لعبت بي. جمعت المال من حله ومن غير حله ثم خلفته لغيري. فالمهنأة له ، والتبعة علي . فاحذروا مثل ما حل بي » ووجه الاستدلال : أنه عليه السلام . حكم بأن الجسد الميت المحمول على النعش حال كونه كذلك ، ترفرف روحه فوق النعش ، وتقول : « يا أهلي. ويا ولدي . لا تلعين بكم الدنيا . ، كما لعبت بي ، ومعلوم : أن الأهل والولد ، ما كانا إلا كذلك الإنسان . فلما قال الروح المترفرف هذا الكلام ثبت أن الإنسان [ ما كان إلا ذلك الروح . ولما كان ذلك الروح باقياً ، وجب كون ذلك الإنسان ] باقياً حال ما كان الجسد ميتاً محمولاً على النعش . وذلك من أظهر الدلائل على أن الإنسان شيء مغاير لهذا الجسد ، ومغاير لجميع أبعاضه وأجزائه ويقرب من هذا الدليل : ما روي أنه عليه السلام ألقى جثث القتلى يوم بدر في وهدة ، ثم نادى بأعلى صوته ، وقال : « لقد وجدنا ما وعدنا ربنا : حقاً . فهل وجدتم ما وعدكم ربكم حقاً ؟ ، فقيل له : يا رسول الله : أتخاطب الموتى ؟ فقال : ( إنهم أقوى سمعاً وفهماً منكم ، وهذا يدل على أنهم فاهمون عاقلون مدركون ، حال كون تلك الأبدان ميتة متمزقة متفرقة . والحي مغاير لما في هذا وفي غيره من النطق والإدراك وحسن المحاولة وتحصيل المعقولات إلى أن يموت.
The sixth proof: His statement, peace be upon him, in one of his sermons: 'When the deceased is carried on his bier, his soul flutters above the bier and says: O my family, O my children, let not the world deceive you as it deceived me. I gathered wealth from its lawful and unlawful sources and then left it to others. Its enjoyment is for them, and its burden is upon me. So beware of what has befallen me.' And the aspect of the evidence: He, peace be upon him, judged that the dead body carried on the bier, while it is such, its soul flutters above the bier and says: 'O my family, O my children, let not the world deceive you as it deceived me.' And it is known that the family and children are only so for the human being. So when the fluttering soul said this speech, it is established that the human being was only that soul. And since that soul remains, it is necessary that that human being remains while the body is dead and carried on the bier. And that is among the clearest evidences that the human being is something other than this body, and other than all its limbs and parts. And close to this evidence is what was narrated: that he, peace be upon him, threw the corpses of the slain on the day of Badr into a pit, then called out with a loud voice and said: 'We have certainly found what our Lord promised us to be true. Have you found what your Lord promised you to be true?' It was said to him: O Messenger of God, do you address the dead? He said: 'They are stronger in hearing and understanding than you.' And this indicates that they are understanding, rational, perceiving while those bodies are dead, torn apart, scattered. And the living being is different from what is in this and other than it of speech, perception, good attempt, and acquisition of intelligibles until death.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage presents the sixth proof, consisting of two hadiths. The first hadith describes the soul of the deceased hovering over the bier and speaking to its family. The author argues that the soul's speech shows that the true identity of the human being is that soul, not the dead body. Since the soul persists, the human being persists even after bodily death. The second hadith about the Battle of Badr supports this: the Prophet addressed the dead polytheists, and they heard and understood, even though their bodies were dead and dismembered. This proves that the perceiving, rational self (al-hayy) is different from the body. The author concludes that the living being is distinct from the body and its faculties.

Key Terms
روح
نعش
ترفرف
قتلى بدر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Death is the end of the human being; the body and soul cease together.
Correction: The hadiths show the soul survives and remains conscious, proving the human being is not the body but the soul that continues after death.

Checkpoint
What does the first hadith about the soul hovering over the bier prove according to the author?
A) The soul becomes unconscious after death.
B) The soul is the true self that survives the body.
C) The soul ceases to exist at death.
D) The body can speak after death.

Key Takeaway
The soul's survival after death is proven by prophetic reports showing the soul remains conscious and active, identifying it as the true self distinct from the body.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

The Sixth Proof: The Soul Hovers Over the Bier
Fakhr al-Din al-Razi presents the sixth proof for the soul's distinctness from the body using a hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a hadith about the soul hovering over the bier serves as proof that the soul is distinct from the body and survives after death.

Core Idea
The speaking spirit after death proves the soul is not the body.

In this proof, Fakhr al-Din al-Razi draws on a prophetic hadith that describes the soul of a deceased person hovering over the bier and addressing its family. The fact that the soul speaks and warns its kin indicates that the true human identity is the soul, which continues to exist after the body's death. This passage provides a vivid argument for the soul's distinctness and survival.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its context
Read the Arabic passage, focusing on the hadith about the soul hovering over the bier. Note that the Prophet attributes speech to the soul after death.
The hadith is quoted directly from the Prophet's sermon.
2
Understand the inference chain
The author extracts a logical inference from the hadith: the soul speaks, so it is the real person; since it persists after death, the human being is not the body.
Identify each step from the hadith statement to the conclusion.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Consider how this proof ties into the broader argument that the soul is a separate substance from the body. Ask yourself what assumptions about identity are required for this proof to work.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اللفظ في هذه المرتبة أيضاً . وحيث خص هذه المرتبة بهذا اللفظ ، دل ذلك على أن الروح ليس من جنس الأجسام .

الحجة السادسة : قوله عليه السلام في بعض خطبه : « إذا حمل الميت على نعشه رفرفت روحه فوق النعش ، وتقول : يا أهلي ويا ولدي . لا تلعبن بكم الدنيا ، كما لعبت بي. جمعت المال من حله ومن غير حله ثم خلفته لغيري. فالمهنأة له ، والتبعة علي . فاحذروا مثل ما حل بي

ووجه الاستدلال : أنه عليه السلام . حكم بأن الجسد الميت المحمول على النعش حال كونه كذلك ، ترفرف روحه فوق النعش ، وتقول : « يا أهـلي. ويا ولدي . لا تلعين بكم الدنيا ، كما لعبت بي ، ومعلوم : أن الأهل والولد ، ما كانا إلا كذلك الإنسان . فلما قال الروح المترفرف هذا الكلام ثبت أن الإنسان ما كان إلا ذلك الروح . ولما كان ذلك الروح باقياً ، وجب كون ذلك الإنسان باقياً حال ما كان الجسد ميتاً محمولاً على النعش . وذلك من أظهر الدلائل على أن الإنسان شيء مغاير لهذا الجسد ، ومغاير لجميع أبعاضه وأجزائه
The word (al-lafẓ) in this rank as well. And since he specified this rank with this word, that indicates that the spirit (al-rūḥ) is not of the same genus as bodies.

The sixth proof: His statement, peace be upon him, in one of his sermons: 'When the deceased is carried on his bier, his spirit flutters above the bier and says: O my family and O my children. Do not let the world deceive you as it deceived me. I gathered wealth from its permissible and from its impermissible, then I left it for others. So the ease is for him, and the burden is upon me. So beware of what has befallen me.'

And the aspect of inference: that he, peace be upon him, judged that the dead body carried on the bier, while being so, his spirit flutters above the bier and says: 'O my family, O my children, do not let the world deceive you as it deceived me.' And it is known that family and children are nothing but the human being. So when the fluttering spirit spoke this speech, it was established that the human being is [nothing but] that spirit. And since that spirit is enduring, it is necessary that that human being is enduring while his body is dead and carried on the bier. And that is among the clearest evidences that the human being is something other than this body and other than all its parts and limbs.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage is the sixth proof offered by the author for the distinctness and survival of the soul. It begins with a concluding remark from a previous argument, stating that the word 'spirit' (rūḥ) in this context is specifically used for this rank, indicating that the spirit is not of the same genus as bodies. Then the author presents the sixth proof: a hadith from the Prophet describing how the spirit of a deceased person hovers over the bier and speaks, warning its family. The author points out that the spirit speaks and refers to the family, which demonstrates that the true human identity is the spirit, not the body. Since the spirit continues to exist and speak after death, it must be something separate from the physical body. This is explicit evidence that the human being is other than the body and its parts.

Key Terms
الروح
الجسد
الاستدلال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith about the soul hovering over the bier is only an allegory and not a literal description of the soul's activity after death.
Correction: The author takes the hadith as literal evidence that the soul is a distinct entity that survives bodily death. If it were merely allegorical, the proof would lose its force as rational evidence for the soul's distinctness.

Checkpoint

A) The body continues to feel pain after death.
B) The spirit is of the same genus as the body.
C) The human being is primarily the spirit and not the body.
D) The spirit only exists while the body is alive.

Key Takeaway
This hadith provides explicit evidence that the soul survives bodily death and is the true essence of the human being.

The Prophet's Address to the Dead at Badr: A Proof for the Soul's Survival
Al-Razi presents a near proof based on the Prophet's address to the dead at Badr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's address to the dead at Badr serves as a rational proof for the soul's existence independent of the body.

Core Idea
The dead at Badr heard the Prophet, proving the soul lives on.

Al-Razi presents a second proof, based on a famous incident from the Battle of Badr. When the Prophet spoke to the slain polytheists and affirmed they could hear him, it demonstrated that the dead retain perception. This leads to the conclusion that the human being is more than just the physical body.

Guided Path
1
Read the narration
Read the passage about the Prophet throwing the corpses into a pit and addressing them. Notice the exact words he spoke.
The narration is from the Battle of Badr.
2
Understand the objection
Consider the objection posed to the Prophet: 'Are you addressing the dead?' This shows that the living might think it futile to speak to corpses.
3
Examine the Prophet's response
The Prophet replies that the dead hear better and understand more than the living. This is the core of the proof.
It indicates the dead have perception beyond the physical.
4
Follow Al-Razi's deduction
Al-Razi argues that since the dead can perceive despite their bodies being dead and torn, the perceiving entity must be non-material. Therefore, the human being (soul) is distinct from the body.
This is a logical argument from the narrated event.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقرب من هذا الدليل : ما روي أنه عليه السلام ألقى جثث القتلى يوم بدر في وهدة ، ثم نادى بأعلى صوته ، وقال : « لقد وجدنا ما وعدنا ربنا : حقاً . فهل وجدتم ما وعدكم ربكم حقاً ؟ ، فقيل له : يا رسول الله : أتخاطب الموتى ؟ فقال : ( إنهم أقوى سمعاً وفهماً منكم )، وهذا يدل على أنهم فاهمون عاقلون مدركون ، حال كون تلك الأبدان ميتة متمزقة متفرقة . والحي مغاير لما هو غير حي . فوجب أن يكون الإنسان مغايراً لهذه الجثث ولجميع أجزائها وأقسامها .
And near to this proof is what is narrated that he, peace be upon him, threw the corpses of the slain on the day of Badr into a pit, then called out with a loud voice and said: 'We have indeed found what our Lord promised us to be true. Have you found what your Lord promised you to be true?' It was said to him: O Messenger of God, are you addressing the dead? He said: 'They hear better and understand more than you.' And this indicates that they are comprehending, rational, and perceptive while those bodies are dead, torn apart, and scattered. And the living is other than what is not living. So it is necessary that the human being is other than these corpses and all their parts and divisions.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage is a second, closely related proof. It cites the well-known incident from the Battle of Badr where the Prophet addressed the slain polytheists in their grave, and when questioned, replied that they could hear. The author argues that since the dead were capable of understanding and perception even though their bodies were destroyed, the perceiving entity must be distinct from the body. This further supports the conclusion that the human being is not identical to the physical body.

Correction: The Prophet explicitly stated that the dead hear and understand, showing he was addressing them directly and they could perceive.

The Seventh Proof: Scriptural Descriptions Demand a Surviving Soul
Al-Razi presents the seventh proof based on scriptural descriptions of afterlife.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the multitude of scriptural texts about afterlife rewards and punishments provides a compelling proof for the soul's distinction from the body and its survival after death.

Core Idea
Scriptural descriptions of afterlife experiences imply a non-bodily subject that survives death.

Fakhr al-Din al-Razi now turns to a proof based on the sheer volume of scriptural reports about the afterlife. He argues that these texts cannot be mere metaphors because they describe real experiences of pleasure and pain, yet the bodies we see are clearly insentient after death. This forces the conclusion that there is a soul distinct from the body that continues to perceive and understand.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation. Let the author's own argument come through before interpreting.
Notice the concise, logical style of al-Razi.
2
Identify the key components
Identify the premise about scriptural reports, the observation about dead bodies, the logical contradiction, and the conclusion about the soul.
This proof has four clear logical stages.
3
Reflect on the multitude of texts
Al-Razi emphasizes that the verses and reports are beyond counting. Ask yourself why this cumulative evidence strengthens the argument.
The sheer volume makes metaphorical interpretation less plausible.
4
Connect to earlier rational proofs
Consider how this scriptural proof complements previous rational arguments for the soul's distinction and survival.
This proof relies on transmitted knowledge, not pure reason.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السابعة : كل خبر ورد في بيان أن أهل الطاعات وصلوا إلى الخيرات والراحات. وأن أهل المعاصي وصلوا إلى العذاب والبلاء فهو بعينه يدل على أن النفس غير البدن ، وعلى أنها لا تموت بموت البدن ، وعلى أنها تبقى مدركة عاقلة فاهمة بعد موت البدن . وذلك لأنا نشاهد هذه الأبدان متفرقة متمزقة ، خالية عن الحس والإدراك والشعور . فالقول بإثبات الحس والمعرفة والإدراك لها ، مكابرة في الضروريات. ثم إن هذه النصوص دالة على أن أولئك الناس ، واصلون إما إلى الخيرات والسعادات وإما إلى الشرور والآفات والعلم الضروري حاصل بأن الحي العاقل الفاهم مغاير لما ليس كذلك . وهذا يفيد القطع بأن النفس غير البدن ، وعلى أنها باقية بعد موت البدن . ولما كانت الآيات والأخبار الدالة على وصول السعداء إلى منازل الخيرات ، ووصول الأشقياء إلى دركات الآفات، خارجة عن العد والإحصاء ، لا جرم كانت الدلائل السمعية الدالة على أن النفس غير البدن ، وغير عضو من هذه الأعضاء خارجة عن العد والإحصاء والله أعلم .
The seventh proof: Every report that has come concerning that the people of obedience have attained to good things and comforts, and that the people of disobedience have attained to punishment and affliction, it in itself indicates that the soul (al-nafs) is other than the body, and that it does not die with the death of the body, and that it remains perceptive, rational, and understanding after the death of the body. That is because we observe these bodies scattered and torn apart, devoid of sensation, perception, and consciousness. So claiming the affirmation of sensation, knowledge, and perception for them is a contradiction of evident truths. Then these texts indicate that those people are reaching either good things and felicities or evils and afflictions. And necessary knowledge is obtained that the living, rational, understanding being is other than what is not like that. And this yields certainty that the soul is other than the body, and that it remains after the death of the body. And since the verses and reports that indicate the arrival of the felicitous to the abodes of good things and the arrival of the wretched to the depths of afflictions are beyond counting and enumeration, inevitably the transmitted proofs indicating that the soul is other than the body and other than any of these organs are beyond counting and enumeration. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage is the seventh proof, based on the many scriptural texts that describe the afterlife rewards and punishments. The author argues that these texts necessarily imply that the soul (nafs) survives the body, because the bodies we see are lifeless and insentient, yet the texts speak of the dead experiencing pleasure or pain. This would be a contradiction unless the soul is a distinct, enduring entity. The author emphasizes that the multitude of such texts (from Qur'an and hadith) provides overwhelming cumulative evidence for the distinction and survival of the soul.

Misconception: That the texts about afterlife can be interpreted as purely metaphorical without implying a real subject of experience.
Correction: Al-Razi argues that the multitude of texts describing real pleasure and pain for the dead forces a literal interpretation, which in turn requires a subject (the soul) distinct from the insentient body.

Razi's Proof from Self-Attribution: The Soul Is Not the Body
Razi proves the soul is not the body via self-attribution absurdity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's argument that if the soul were identical to the body, then saying 'my body' would be a self-contradiction, proving the soul is distinct.

Core Idea
If the soul were the body, 'my body' would be a thing attributing itself to itself—impossible.

Razi here uses a crisp logical proof to show that the soul cannot be identical to the body. He argues that our everyday language about 'my body' already implies a distinction between the self and the body, because otherwise such phrases would be meaningless self-references. Let's unpack this argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the flow of the argument. Notice how Razi sets up a conditional scenario.
2
Identify the key distinction
Find where Razi distinguishes between participation (mushāraka) and opposition (mukhālafa). Understand that difference suffices for attribution.
This is the backdrop for the hypothetical.
3
Follow the hypothetical
Trace the conditional: if the soul = body, then 'my body' is self-attribution. Recognize why that is impossible (muḥāl).
Think about why self-reference in one consideration is logically absurd.
4
Draw the conclusion
Conclude that since the hypothetical leads to impossibility, the soul cannot be identical to the body.
This is a modus tollens argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المشاركة غير ما به المخالفة ، فقد حصلت المغايرة من هذا الوجه ، فلا جرم كفت هذه المغايرة في صحة هذه الإضافة. أما لو كانت النفس عبارة عن مجموع هذا البدن ، أو عن عضو مخصوص ، فحينئذ كانت تلك النفس عين (۱) ذلك البدن ، وذلك البدن عين تلك النفس ، فكان قوله ( بدني وقلبي ) يوجب إضافة الشيء إلى نفسه بالاعتبار الواحد . وذلك محال . فظهر الفرق [ بين البابين . والله أعلم (۲) ] .
Participation is other than opposition, so difference is obtained from this aspect, so inevitably this difference suffices for the validity of this attribution. But if the soul were the totality of this body, or a particular organ, then that soul would be identical to that body, and that body identical to that soul, so his saying 'my body and my heart' would necessitate attributing a thing to itself under one consideration. And that is impossible. So the difference between the two sections became clear. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage is a proof that the soul (nafs) is not identical to the body. The author first establishes a distinction between participation (mushāraka) and opposition (mukhālafa), noting that difference suffices for the validity of attribution (iḍāfa). Then he argues hypothetically: if the soul were the entire body or a specific organ, then the soul would be identical ('ayn) to the body. In that case, saying 'my body' would be attributing a thing to itself under one and the same consideration, which is impossible (muḥāl). Therefore, the soul must be distinct from the body. The proof shows the absurdity of self-reference as a logical refutation of the identity claim.

Key Terms
النفس
البدن
الإضافة
المغايرة
المشاركة
المخالفة
عين
محال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument is just linguistic wordplay and doesn't prove anything about the soul's essence.
Correction: Razi's argument uses the logical principle that self-attribution is impossible, which is a non-linguistic metaphysical truth. The absurdity of self-reference reveals the ontological distinction between soul and body.

Checkpoint

C) The soul would be mortal like the body.
D) The soul would be a material substance.

Key Takeaway
Razi uses the impossibility of self-reference to prove that the soul cannot be identical to the body, establishing a clear ontological distinction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
Razi proves that 'my body' is a valid phrase only because the soul is not the body. Do you actually think of your body as a possession you are responsible for, or do you let it control you? How can you start treating it as a trust from your Lord?
?
The argument shows that self-reference to one's own essence is impossible. Yet you refer to your own actions and thoughts every day. Are you living in the reality that your 'self' is known only to Allah, or are you trying to define yourself through worldly labels? What step can you take today to deepen your awareness of your soul's distinct reality?
