Ibn Sina's Proof Against Metempsychosis
Ibn Sina presents a proof against metempsychosis based on the creation of souls and the necessity of a temporal condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ibn Sina's argument that metempsychosis leads to the impossibility of two souls in one body.

Core Idea
Metempsychosis would require two souls in one body, which our own experience contradicts.

Ibn Sina presents a concise proof against the transmigration of souls. He builds on two premises: souls are created, and their cause is eternal. He then shows that if metempsychosis were true, a single body would have to host two souls—an impossible situation. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice the structure of Ibn Sina's argument.
The proof is succinct but requires attention to the logical steps.
2
Identify the two premises
Find the two premises: that human souls are created (haditha) and that their cause is eternal (qadima). Understand why Ibn Sina asserts these.
These are taken as established from earlier discussions.
3
Understand the temporal condition
Ibn Sina explains that an eternal cause can produce a temporal effect only if a temporal condition is fulfilled. In this case, the condition is the occurrence of the body.
This concept is central to Ibn Sina's emanationist framework.
4
Follow the impossibility
If metempsychosis occurred, a transmigrating soul and a newly emanated soul would both attach to the same body, resulting in two souls. This is impossible because we each experience ourselves as one soul.
The proof relies on self-evident experience.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واحتج الشيخ الرئيس أبو علي بن سينا على فساد القول بالتناسخ بدليلين (الحجة الأولى: قال: إنه ثبت أن النفوس البشرية حادثة، وثبت أن علتها قديمة، والموجود القديم لا يكون علة للشيء المحدث إلا إذا كان تأثيره فيه موقوفاً على شرط حادث وذلك الشرط الحادث وهو حدوث البدن. فعلى هذا إذا حدث بدن وجب أن يفيض عن واجب الصور نفس، فلو تعلق بذلك البدن نفس على سبيل التناسخ وتعلقت به هذه النفوس الحادثة أيضاً لزم أن يتعلق بذلك البدن الواحد نفسان، وهذا محال لأن كل أحد يجد نفسه نفساً واحدة لا نفسين. والاعتراض عليه من وجوه: الأول: لا نسلم أن النفس حادثة. وذلك لأن الدليل الذي ذكرتم في إثبات حدوث النفس كان موقوفاً على إبطال التناسخ ثم إنكم بنيتم دليلكم في إبطال التناسخ على حدوث النفس فيقع الدور وهو باطل. والاعتراض الثاني: سلمنا أن النفس حادثة فلم قلتم إن المؤثر في وجود النفس علة موجبة؟ ولم لا يجوز أن يكون المؤثر فيها فاعلاً مختاراً فيخلق تلك النفوس والأرواح في أي وقت شاء وأراد؟ وعلى هذا التقدير فلا يمكنكم أن تقولوا إن حدوث البدن يقتضي حدوث النفس وعند هذا ينتقل الكلام من هذه المسألة إلى مسألة أخرى وهي مسألة الموجب والقادر. والاعتراض الثالث: هب أن النفس حادثة وأن المؤثر في وجودها علة قديمة موجبة بالذات وأن فيضان هذه النفس عن تلك العلة القديمة مشروط بشرط حادث فلم قلتم إن ذلك الشرط الحادث ليس إلا المزاج الحادث؟ وما الدليل على هذا التعيين؟ بل ههنا احتمالات أخرى سوى ذلك فأحدها: أن يقال إنه حصل نفس أو عقل وله تعضلات منتقلة معقول إلى معقول ومن إدراك إلى إدراك والشرط في فيضان هذه النفس الحادثة عن تلك العلة القديمة حدوث تعقل خاص وإدراك خاص في ذلك العقل أو النفس وعلى هذا التقدير تكون النفس حادثة لا لحدوث الأمزجة. وثانيها: أن يقال الشرط لحدوث تلك النفوس عن تلك العلة القديمة وصول الشمس أو سائر الكواكب إلى دقائق أو درجات معينة من الفلك. وثالثها: أن يقال الشرط لحدوث تلك النفوس طالع المسقط أو شيء آخر يشبه ذلك. وبالجملة: فعليكم إقامة الدليل على أنه لا سبب لفيضان النفس المعينة عن تلك العلة القديمة إلا حدوث هذه الأمزجة.
And the chief master Abu Ali ibn Sina argued for the corruption of the doctrine of metempsychosis (al-tanasukh) with two proofs [The first proof: He said: It is established that human souls are created (haditha), and it is established that their cause is eternal (qadima), and the eternal existent cannot be a cause for a created thing unless its effect in it is dependent on a temporal condition (shart hadith) and that temporal condition is the occurrence of the body. So on this, when a body occurs, a soul must emanate from the Necessary of Forms; so if a soul were attached to that body by way of metempsychosis and these created souls also attached to it, it would be necessary that two souls attach to that single body, and this is impossible because every person finds himself as one soul, not two souls. And the objection to it is from several aspects: The first: We do not concede that the soul is created. That is because the proof you mentioned in establishing the creation of the soul was dependent on refuting metempsychosis, then you built your proof in refuting metempsychosis on the creation of the soul, so circularity (al-dawr) occurs, and it is invalid. The second objection: We concede that the soul is created, but why do you say that the effecter in the existence of the soul is a necessitating cause (illa mujiba)? And why may it not be that the effecter in it is a free agent (fa'il mukhtar), creating those souls and spirits whenever He wills and intends? And on this estimation, you cannot say that the occurrence of the body necessitates the occurrence of the soul, and here the discussion moves from this issue to another issue, which is the issue of the necessitating cause and the powerful agent (al-mujib wa al-qadir). The third objection: Grant that the soul is created and that the effecter in its existence is an eternal cause necessitating by essence, and that the emanation of this soul from that eternal cause is conditional upon a temporal condition; so why do you say that that temporal condition is nothing but the temperament (al-mizaj) that occurs? And what is the proof for this specification? Rather, there are other possibilities besides that: One of them: It is said that there is a soul or intellect that has graduated movements moving from intelligible to intelligible and from perception to perception, and the condition for the emanation of this created soul from that eternal cause is the occurrence of a specific intellection and specific perception in that intellect or soul, and on this estimation the soul is created not due to the occurrence of temperaments. The second: It is said that the condition for the occurrence of those souls from that eternal cause is the arrival of the sun or the rest of the planets to specific minutes or degrees of the sphere. The third: It is said that the condition for the occurrence of those souls is the ascendant of the birthplace or something else like that. In summary: You must provide the proof that there is no cause for the emanation of the specific soul from that eternal cause except the occurrence of these temperaments.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage presents Ibn Sina's first proof against the doctrine of metempsychosis (tanasukh) and three objections raised against it. The proof begins from two premises: that human souls are created (haditha) and that their cause is eternal (qadima). An eternal cause, according to Ibn Sina, can only produce a temporal effect if a temporal condition (shart hadith) is fulfilled—in this case, the occurrence of a body. Thus, when a body arises, a soul must necessarily emanate from the Necessary of Forms (Wajib al-Suwar). If a soul were to transmigrate into that body, then two souls would attach to one body: the transmigrating soul and the newly emanated soul. This is impossible, as we each experience ourselves as a single soul. The first objection attacks the premise that the soul is created, claiming circularity: the proof of the soul's creation depends on refuting metempsychosis, yet the refutation of metempsychosis uses the soul's creation. The second objection concedes the soul's creation but questions why the cause must be necessitating; if God acts as a free agent, He can create souls at will without the body's condition. This shifts the debate to the issue of determinism vs. free will. The third objection grants all premises but challenges the identification of the temporal condition with the body's temperament; it offers alternative possibilities such as intellectual progress, astronomical alignments, or astrological factors. The objector demands evidence that the temperament is the sole condition.

Key Terms
النفوس البشرية (human souls)
حادثة (created)
علة قديمة (eternal cause)
شرط حادث (temporal condition)
البدن (body)
واجب الصور (Necessary of Forms)
نفسان (two souls)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think Ibn Sina's proof assumes the soul is pre-existent and eternal.
Correction: The proof explicitly states that souls are created (haditha), not eternal. The argument relies on the soul's temporal origination.

Checkpoint
What is the central impossibility Ibn Sina argues would result from metempsychosis?
A) The soul would be eternal.
B) Two souls would coexist in one body.
C) The body would have no soul.
D) The cause would become temporal.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Sina's proof demonstrates that metempsychosis would require two souls in one body, which contradicts our direct experience of having a single soul.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have direct experience of having a single soul. If your soul is uniquely created for this body, what does that imply about the personal responsibility you carry? How will you honor that uniqueness starting today?
?
Ibn Sina's proof shows that no other soul can inhabit your body. How does that confront the excuses you make about not being able to change? What would it mean to accept that only you can shape your spiritual destiny?
?
If every soul is specifically tied to its body's occurrence, then your existence is not an accident. What are you doing with this life that you would be unable to justify if it were the only one you have? Make a concrete change before you finish this reflection.

Unseen Matters

Three Objections to Ibn Sina's Proof Against Metempsychosis
Three objections are raised against Ibn Sina's proof, attacking circularity, necessitation, and the specific temporal condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three objections raised against Ibn Sina's proof and their implications for the soul and causation.

Core Idea
Objectors challenge Ibn Sina's premises, his necessitarian causation, and his identification of the body's temperament as the sole condition.

Ibn Sina's proof against metempsychosis was not without its critics. Three objections directly target his argument: the first claims circularity, the second questions why the cause must be necessitating rather than a free agent, and the third demands proof that the body's temperament is the only temporal condition. This lesson examines each objection in detail.

Guided Path
1
Read the objections
Read the Arabic passage containing all three objections. Then read the translation. Note that each objection begins with a conditional concession.
The objections are numbered (الاول, الثاني, الثالث).
2
Understand the circularity objection
The first objection points out that Ibn Sina's proof depends on the soul being created, but the proof of the soul's creation itself depends on refuting metempsychosis. This would create a vicious circle.
Circularity (al-dawr) is a logical fallacy.
3
Analyze the free agent objection
The second objection concedes the soul is created but denies that the cause must be necessitating. If God is a free agent, He can create souls without any temporal condition.
This shifts the debate to the issue of whether God acts by necessity or choice.
4
Examine the alternative conditions objection
The third objection grants all premises but argues that the temporal condition could be something other than the body's temperament, such as intellectual progress or astronomical events.
The burden of proof is on Ibn Sina to show why the temperament is the only condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واحتج الشيخ الرئيس أبو علي بن سينا على فساد القول بالتناسخ بدليلين (الحجة الأولى: قال: إنه ثبت أن النفوس البشرية حادثة، وثبت أن علتها قديمة، والموجود القديم لا يكون علة للشيء المحدث إلا إذا كان تأثيره فيه موقوفاً على شرط حادث وذلك الشرط الحادث وهو حدوث البدن. فعلى هذا إذا حدث بدن وجب أن يفيض عن واجب الصور نفس، فلو تعلق بذلك البدن نفس على سبيل التناسخ وتعلقت به هذه النفوس الحادثة أيضاً لزم أن يتعلق بذلك البدن الواحد نفسان، وهذا محال لأن كل أحد يجد نفسه نفساً واحدة لا نفسين. والاعتراض عليه من وجوه: الأول: لا نسلم أن النفس حادثة. وذلك لأن الدليل الذي ذكرتم في إثبات حدوث النفس كان موقوفاً على إبطال التناسخ ثم إنكم بنيتم دليلكم في إبطال التناسخ على حدوث النفس فيقع الدور وهو باطل. والاعتراض الثاني: سلمنا أن النفس حادثة فلم قلتم إن المؤثر في وجود النفس علة موجبة؟ ولم لا يجوز أن يكون المؤثر فيها فاعلاً مختاراً فيخلق تلك النفوس والأرواح في أي وقت شاء وأراد؟ وعلى هذا التقدير فلا يمكنكم أن تقولوا إن حدوث البدن يقتضي حدوث النفس وعند هذا ينتقل الكلام من هذه المسألة إلى مسألة أخرى وهي مسألة الموجب والقادر. والاعتراض الثالث: هب أن النفس حادثة وأن المؤثر في وجودها علة قديمة موجبة بالذات وأن فيضان هذه النفس عن تلك العلة القديمة مشروط بشرط حادث فلم قلتم إن ذلك الشرط الحادث ليس إلا المزاج الحادث؟ وما الدليل على هذا التعيين؟ بل ههنا احتمالات أخرى سوى ذلك فأحدها: أن يقال إنه حصل نفس أو عقل وله تعضلات منتقلة معقول إلى معقول ومن إدراك إلى إدراك والشرط في فيضان هذه النفس الحادثة عن تلك العلة القديمة حدوث تعقل خاص وإدراك خاص في ذلك العقل أو النفس وعلى هذا التقدير تكون النفس حادثة لا لحدوث الأمزجة. وثانيها: أن يقال الشرط لحدوث تلك النفوس عن تلك العلة القديمة وصول الشمس أو سائر الكواكب إلى دقائق أو درجات معينة من الفلك. وثالثها: أن يقال الشرط لحدوث تلك النفوس طالع المسقط أو شيء آخر يشبه ذلك. وبالجملة: فعليكم إقامة الدليل على أنه لا سبب لفيضان النفس المعينة عن تلك العلة القديمة إلا حدوث هذه الأمزجة.
And the chief master Abu Ali ibn Sina argued for the corruption of the doctrine of metempsychosis (al-tanasukh) with two proofs [The first proof: He said: It is established that human souls are created (haditha), and it is established that their cause is eternal (qadima), and the eternal existent cannot be a cause for a created thing unless its effect in it is dependent on a temporal condition (shart hadith) and that temporal condition is the occurrence of the body. So on this, when a body occurs, a soul must emanate from the Necessary of Forms; so if a soul were attached to that body by way of metempsychosis and these created souls also attached to it, it would be necessary that two souls attach to that single body, and this is impossible because every person finds himself as one soul, not two souls. And the objection to it is from several aspects: The first: We do not concede that the soul is created. That is because the proof you mentioned in establishing the creation of the soul was dependent on refuting metempsychosis, then you built your proof in refuting metempsychosis on the creation of the soul, so circularity (al-dawr) occurs, and it is invalid. The second objection: We concede that the soul is created, but why do you say that the effecter in the existence of the soul is a necessitating cause (illa mujiba)? And why may it not be that the effecter in it is a free agent (fa'il mukhtar), creating those souls and spirits whenever He wills and intends? And on this estimation, you cannot say that the occurrence of the body necessitates the occurrence of the soul, and here the discussion moves from this issue to another issue, which is the issue of the necessitating cause and the powerful agent (al-mujib wa al-qadir). The third objection: Grant that the soul is created and that the effecter in its existence is an eternal cause necessitating by essence, and that the emanation of this soul from that eternal cause is conditional upon a temporal condition; so why do you say that that temporal condition is nothing but the temperament (al-mizaj) that occurs? And what is the proof for this specification? Rather, there are other possibilities besides that: One of them: It is said that there is a soul or intellect that has graduated movements moving from intelligible to intelligible and from perception to perception, and the condition for the emanation of this created soul from that eternal cause is the occurrence of a specific intellection and specific perception in that intellect or soul, and on this estimation the soul is created not due to the occurrence of temperaments. The second: It is said that the condition for the occurrence of those souls from that eternal cause is the arrival of the sun or the rest of the planets to specific minutes or degrees of the sphere. The third: It is said that the condition for the occurrence of those souls is the ascendant of the birthplace or something else like that. In summary: You must provide the proof that there is no cause for the emanation of the specific soul from that eternal cause except the occurrence of these temperaments.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage presents Ibn Sina's first proof against the doctrine of metempsychosis (tanasukh) and three objections raised against it. The proof begins from two premises: that human souls are created (haditha) and that their cause is eternal (qadima). An eternal cause, according to Ibn Sina, can only produce a temporal effect if a temporal condition (shart hadith) is fulfilled—in this case, the occurrence of a body. Thus, when a body arises, a soul must necessarily emanate from the Necessary of Forms (Wajib al-Suwar). If a soul were to transmigrate into that body, then two souls would attach to one body: the transmigrating soul and the newly emanated soul. This is impossible, as we each experience ourselves as a single soul. The first objection attacks the premise that the soul is created, claiming circularity: the proof of the soul's creation depends on refuting metempsychosis, yet the refutation of metempsychosis uses the soul's creation. The second objection concedes the soul's creation but questions why the cause must be necessitating; if God acts as a free agent, He can create souls at will without the body's condition. This shifts the debate to the issue of determinism vs. free will. The third objection grants all premises but challenges the identification of the temporal condition with the body's temperament; it offers alternative possibilities such as intellectual progress, astronomical alignments, or astrological factors. The objector demands evidence that the temperament is the sole condition.

Key Terms
الدور (circularity)
فاعل مختار (free agent)
موجب (necessitating cause)
المزاج (temperament)
تعقل (intellection)
طالع المسقط (ascendant)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the objections are easily dismissed, but they raise deep issues about circularity, divine freedom, and causation.
Correction: Each objection points to a significant assumption in Ibn Sina's argument that is not universally accepted.

Checkpoint
What is the main point of the first objection?
A) The soul is not created.
B) The proof involves circular reasoning.
C) The cause must be a free agent.
D) The body's temperament is not the only condition.

Key Takeaway
The three objections challenge Ibn Sina's proof by attacking its logical consistency, its assumption of necessitation, and its identification of the body's temperament as the unique condition for the soul's creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever defended a belief using an argument that you later realized was circular? How did you respond when someone pointed that out? What does this passage teach you about the importance of logical consistency in your own faith?
?
Do you tend to think of God as a necessitating cause (like a natural law) or as a free agent who acts by His will? How might this affect your relationship with Him? Are you comfortable with the idea that He creates souls without any pre-existing condition?
?
When you read the third objection, did you feel that the alternatives (astronomy, astrology) were far-fetched? Yet the objector demands proof. How often do you accept explanations without demanding evidence? In your own spiritual life, are there areas where you have assumed something is the only way without considering other possibilities?

Third objection: alternative conditions for the soul's emanation
Transition to causality issue and third objection listing alternative conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third objection's challenge to the claim that temperament is the exclusive temporal condition for the soul's emanation from the eternal cause, and the three alternative conditions proposed.

Core Idea
The soul's emanation may depend on cognitive, celestial, or astrological conditions, not just the body's temperament.

This passage introduces a key objection against the argument that the soul's temporal origination is necessarily tied to the body's temperament. After noting a transition to the broader issue of causality, the objector grants the core premises but questions why temperament must be the unique condition. Three alternative possibilities are presented, shifting the burden of proof back to the proponents of the temperament theory.

Guided Path
1
Understand the transition and assumption
Notice how the discussion moves from the soul's origination to the issue of the necessitating cause and the powerful. The objector grants that the soul is originated and that its cause is an eternal necessitating cause, but questions the specific condition.
This is a common dialectical move: granting premises to challenge the conclusion.
2
Identify the three alternative conditions
Read each alternative carefully: the first involves a particular intellection in the soul itself, the second involves celestial positions, the third involves the astrological ascendant. How do these differ from the temperament condition?
The first alternative is particularly interesting because it locates the condition within the soul's own activity.
3
Appreciate the burden of proof
The objection concludes by demanding that the proponents of the temperament theory prove that no other condition is possible. This is a strong challenge that shifts the discussion to a higher level of proof.
In kalam, the burden of proof is often on the one making the positive claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تقولوا : إن حدوث البدن يقتضي حدوث النفس وعند هذا ] ينتقل هذا الكلام من هذه المسألة إلى مسألة [ أخرى . وهي مسألة ] الموجب والقادر . والاعتراض الثالث : هب أن النفس حادثة ، وأن المؤثر في وجودها علة قديمة موجبة بالذات، وأن فيضان هذه النفس عن تلك العلة القديمة مشروط بشرط حادث . فلم قلتم : إن ذلك الشرط الحادث ليس إلا المزاج الحادث ؟ وما الدليل على هذا التعيين ؟ بل ههنا احتمالات أخرى سوى ذلك
فأحدها: أن يقال : إنه حصل نفس أو عقل ، وله تعضلات منتقلة معقول إلى معقول . ومن إدراك إلى إدراك . والشرط في فيضان هذه النفس الحادثة عن تلك العلة القديمة : حدوث تعقل خاص [ وإدراك خاص ] في ذلك العقل أو النفس . وعلى هذا التقدير تكون النفس حادثة ، لا لحدوث الأمزجة.
وثانيها : أن يقال : الشرط لحدوث تلك النفوس عن تلك العلة القديمة ، وصول الشمس أو سائر الكواكب إلى دقائق أو درجات معينة من الفلك
•
وثالثها : [ أن يقال ] الشرط لحدوث تلك النفوس طالع المسقط ، أو شيء آخر يشبه ذلك
وبالجملة : فعليكم إقامة الدليل على أنه لا سبب لفيضان النفس المعينة عن تلك العلة القديمة ، إلا حدوث هذه الأمزجة .
You say: The temporal origination of the body necessitates the temporal origination of the soul. And at this point, this discourse moves from this issue to another issue, which is the issue of the necessitating cause and the powerful. And the third objection: Suppose that the soul is temporally originated, and that the effective cause in its existence is an eternal cause necessitating by essence, and that the emanation of this soul from that eternal cause is conditioned by a temporal condition. Why then do you say that this temporal condition is nothing but the temporal temperament? And what is the proof for this specification? Rather, there are other possibilities besides that. One of them: It is said that a soul or intellect has come to be, and it has movements that transfer from one intelligible to another, and from one perception to another. And the condition for the emanation of this temporally originated soul from that eternal cause is the occurrence of a particular intellection [and a particular perception] in that intellect or soul. On this assumption, the soul is temporally originated, not due to the occurrence of temperaments. The second: It is said that the condition for the temporal origination of those souls from that eternal cause is the arrival of the sun or other planets to specific minutes or degrees of the sphere. The third: [It is said that] the condition for the temporal origination of those souls is the ascendant of the place of birth, or something else similar to that. In summary: It is incumbent upon you to provide evidence that there is no cause for the emanation of a particular soul from that eternal cause except the occurrence of these temperaments.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage presents the third objection to the argument that the soul's temporal origination is tied to the temperament of the body. The author begins by noting a transition in the discussion from the previous issue to a new issue concerning the necessitating cause (الموجب) and the powerful (القادر). Then the objection is laid out: Even if we grant that the soul is temporally originated and that it emanates from an eternal necessitating cause under some temporal condition, why must that condition be the temperament? The opponent demands proof for this specification and then offers three alternative conditions. First, the condition could be a particular act of intellection or perception within the soul or intellect itself, making the soul temporally originated due to its own cognitive acts, not bodily temperament. Second, the condition could be astronomical, such as the precise position of the sun or planets. Third, the condition could be astrological, such as the ascendant at birth. The conclusion demands that the proponent of the temperament theory must prove that no other condition is possible.

Key Terms

العلة القديمة
الموجب والقادر
المزاج
التعقل الخاص

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The third objection denies that the soul is temporally originated.
Correction: The objection actually accepts that the soul is originated but questions the exclusive role of temperament.

Key Takeaway
The third objection forces defenders of the temperament theory to prove that no other temporal condition could serve as the occasion for the soul's emanation, broadening the scope of the debate.

The Fourth Objection: Differences in Temperament and Soul
The fourth objection argues that even if temperament is the condition, differences in temperament and soul prevent universal applicability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the fourth objection undermines the claim that a single temperament can universally serve as the cause for any soul.

Core Idea
Differences in temperament and soul break the one-size-fits-all causal link.

The discussion now turns to a sophisticated concession: even if we grant that temperament is the temporal cause, the argument fails to prove universal applicability. The objector introduces crucial distinctions among temperaments and souls, showing that what holds for one case may not hold for another. This sets the stage for understanding the limits of causal reasoning in kalām.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the concessive opening: 'We grant that... However, we say...'
2
Identify what is conceded and attacked
The objector grants that the temporal cause is temperament. Then attacks the universality. Recognize strategy: concession does not mean acceptance of the full argument.
3
Understand why differences matter
Temperaments differ, and souls are not proven equal in essence. If both are variable, a temperament suited to one soul may not suit another.
This destroys the assumption of a universal mapping.
4
See how the proof is invalidated
The conclusion: from one case of receptivity, we cannot infer another. Hence the original proof fails.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والاعتراض الرابع : سلمنا أن ذلك السبب الحادث هو المزاج الحادث . إلا أنا نقول : الأمزجة مختلفة . ولم يثبت بالدليل كون النفوس متساوية في الماهية. وإذا كانت الأمزجة مختلفة ، وكانت النفوس مختلفة ، لم يلزم من كون هذا المزاج الحادث ، قابلاً للنفس التناسخية : كونه قابلا للنفس الحادثة الأخرى. وحينئذ يبطل هذا الدليل
And the fourth objection: We grant that that temporal cause is the temporal temperament. However, we say: Temperaments are different, and it has not been proven by evidence that souls are equal in essence. If temperaments are different and souls are different, then it does not follow from the fact that this temporal temperament is receptive to the transmigrating soul that it is receptive to another temporally originated soul. And thus this proof is invalidated.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth objection, which concedes that the temperament is the temporal cause but attacks the universality of the claim. The objector points out that temperaments vary and that souls are not proven to share the same essence. If both temperaments and souls are diverse, then the fact that a particular temperament is suitable for one soul (e.g., the transmigrating soul) does not imply it is suitable for another soul. Therefore, the original proof that temperament necessitates the soul's presence fails because it assumes a one-to-one correspondence that does not hold across different cases.

Key Terms

النفس التناسخية
الماهية
القابلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This objection denies that temperament is a cause at all.
Correction: The objection actually concedes temperament as cause, but attacks the assumption of universal applicability across different temperaments and souls.

Checkpoint

A) Temperaments are not the cause.
B) Souls are all equal in essence.
C) Differences in temperament and soul prevent universal applicability.
D) The transmigrating soul is always present.

Key Takeaway
The fourth objection shows that even if temperament causes the soul, differences in both prevent a universal claim, thereby invalidating the proof.

Fifth Objection: The Uniqueness of Individual Souls
The fifth objection argues against the interchangeability of souls.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the fifth objection argues that even if souls share an essence, their individual distinguishing features prevent interchangeability.

Core Idea
Shared essence does not make souls interchangeable; each soul is unique.

The fifth objection concedes that rational souls share an essential nature but challenges the claim that this makes them interchangeable. It argues that each soul has a distinguishing feature that makes it a composite of commonality and difference. Consequently, a temperament suited for one soul may not be suited for another. This passage presents that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: first a concession, then a series of inferences, then a conclusion.
The objection begins with 'سلمنا' (we grant) – this is a rhetorical concession.
2
Identify the key distinction
Find where the objection introduces the idea that multiplicity arises from something specific to each soul, not from the shared essence alone.
Look for the phrase 'اختصاص كل واحد منها بأمر'.
3
Understand the composite definition
The passage defines each particular soul as a sum of commonality and difference. Grasp why this definition implies uniqueness.
4
Trace the logical conclusion
Follow the argument: because each soul is different, a temperament receptive to one may not be receptive to another. See how this undermines the original proof.
The conclusion is 'فلم يلزم... كونها قابلا للثانية'.
5
Reflect on the objection's force
Consider why this objection is significant: it challenges the assumption that identical essences lead to identical receptivity.
This connects to broader debates about individuation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والاعتراض الخامس : سلمنا : أن النفوس الناطقة متساوية في أصل الماهية ، إلا أن على هذا التقدير لا يحصل التعدد فيها ، إلا لأجل اختصاص كل واحد منها بأمر ، لأجله حصل الامتياز والتعدد . فهذه النفس المعينة : عبارة عن المجموع الحاصل من جهة المشاركة ، ومن جهة المخالفة . وكذلك القول في النفس الثانية. وعلى هذا التقدير فكل واحدة من النفوس المعينة تكون مخالفة للنفس الأخرى ، فلم يلزم من كون المزاج المعين ، قابلاً لأحداهما ، كونه قابلا للثانية . فسقط هذا الدليل
And the fifth objection: We grant that the rational souls are equal in the origin of essence. However, on this assumption, multiplicity among them occurs only because each one is distinguished by something due to which differentiation and multiplicity occur. So this particular soul is an expression of the sum total from the aspect of commonality and from the aspect of difference. And the same is said about the second soul. On this assumption, each of the particular souls is different from the other soul, so it does not follow from the fact that a particular temperament is receptive to one of them that it is receptive to the second. Thus this proof falls.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth objection, which concedes that all rational souls share the same essential nature (أصل الماهية) but argues that individuality arises from a distinguishing feature. Each soul is a composite of what it shares with others and what makes it unique. Therefore, every particular soul is different from every other particular soul. Consequently, a temperament that is receptive to one specific soul is not automatically receptive to another. The objection concludes that the original proof—which assumed that any temperament could host any soul—is invalid.

المجموع

Correction: The objection concedes that souls share an essence but argues that individuality (via a distinguishing feature) prevents interchangeability.

The Sixth Objection: Priority of the Transmigrating Soul
Sixth objection enumerating two reasons for the transmigrating soul's priority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the sixth objection argues that the transmigrating soul is more entitled to a body based on its acquired disposition and prior existence.

Core Idea
A skilled veteran is preferable to a novice — so the transmigrating soul outranks the new soul.

The sixth objection concedes that two particular souls may be equal in essence, but argues that the transmigrating soul has a stronger claim to a given body. This lesson examines two reasons: the acquired disposition from managing previous bodies, and the timing of the new soul's creation. We'll see how the objection uses analogies to make its case, even though it assumes transmigration is possible.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow, then read the literal translation. Notice the two 'وجوه' (aspects) introduced.
The passage ends mid-sentence; focus on the complete arguments given.
2
Understand the first argument: acquired disposition
The transmigrating soul has managed bodies before, acquiring a firm disposition (ملكة راسخة). Compare it to a skilled craftsman vs. a weak child.
This argument rests on the idea that practice leads to ability.
3
Examine the second argument: timing of creation
The newly created soul only comes into existence after the body's temperament is fully formed, implying a delay. Consider how this supports the transmigrating soul's priority.
This argument is incomplete in the passage, but the logic is clear.
4
Reflect on the objection's assumption
The objection assumes transmigration (تناسخ) is possible. In Islamic theology, this is rejected. The objection is hypothetical, meant to be refuted.
Understanding the assumption helps in evaluating the argument's strength.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والاعتراض السادس : سلمنا تساوي النفسين المعينتين بحسب الذوات . فلم لا يجوز أن تختص النفس التناسخية بأصور ، لأجلها تصير هي أولى بذلك البدن ؟ وبيانه من وجوه :
الأول : إن النفس التناسخية ، لما كانت مديرة للأبدان السابقة ، وبقيت مواظبة على ذلك التدبير ، مدة متطاولة ، حصلت لها ملكة راسخة في تدبير الأبدان
وأما هذه النفس الحادثة ، فلم تحصل لها هذه الحالة ، فتكون النفس التناسخية كالرجل القوي الماهر في الصنعة والنفس الحادثة [ لم تحصل لها هذه الحالة. فتكون النفس الحادثة ] كالطفل الضعيف الجاهل بالصنعة ولا شك أن الأول أولى وأقوى .
الثاني : إن النفس الحادثة لا تحدث إلا بعد حصول المزاج وحدوثه على سبيل التمام والكمال . فيكون حدوث هذه النفس متأخراً عن حدوث هذا
And the sixth objection: We grant the equality of the two particular souls in terms of their essences. Why is it not permissible that the transmigrating soul is distinguished by something due to which it becomes more entitled to that body? Its explanation is in aspects: First: Since the transmigrating soul was the manager of previous bodies and remained persistent in that management for a long period, it has acquired a firm disposition in managing bodies. As for this newly originated soul, it has not acquired this state. Thus the transmigrating soul is like a strong man skilled in a craft, and the newly originated soul [has not acquired this state; thus the newly originated soul] is like a weak child ignorant of the craft. There is no doubt that the first is more entitled and stronger. Second: The newly originated soul only comes into existence after the temperament comes to be and occurs perfectly and completely. So the origination of this soul is after the origination of this [temperament].
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage presents the sixth objection, which concedes that two particular souls may be equal in essence but argues that the transmigrating soul has a stronger claim to a given body. Two reasons are given. First, the transmigrating soul has a long history of managing bodies, which gives it a firm disposition (ملكة راسخة) for body management, like a skilled craftsman, whereas the newly created soul is like an ignorant child. Clearly the former is more deserving. Second, the newly created soul only comes into being after the temperament is fully developed, so its origination is later than the temperament's completion. This delay further supports the priority of the soul that already existed. The passage cuts off at this point, but the argument implies that the transmigrating soul is more appropriate for the body.

Key Terms
النفس التناسخية
الملكة الراسخة
تدبير الأبدان
التمام والكمال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the sixth objection proves the transmigrating soul should be given priority over the newly created soul as a valid theological argument.
Correction: The objection assumes the possibility of transmigration (تناسخ), which is rejected in mainstream Islamic theology. It is presented as a hypothetical argument to be refuted.

Checkpoint
What analogy does the sixth objection use to compare the transmigrating soul to the newly created soul?
A) A king versus a servant
B) A strong skilled man versus a weak ignorant child
C) An old building versus a new building
D) Light versus darkness

Key Takeaway
The sixth objection argues for the transmigrating soul's priority based on its acquired disposition and later creation of the new soul, but it rests on the contested assumption of transmigration.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Are you willing to admit that your past may not make you more entitled to Allah's favor, and instead submit to His wisdom in creating you for this specific moment?

The First Argument Against Transmigration: Impossible Consequences
Reductio argument against transmigration with objection and two refutations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first rational argument against the doctrine of transmigration of souls (tanasukh) and how it refutes the objection about equal temperaments.

Core Idea
If two souls exist, they must both attach to both bodies – an obvious absurdity.

The author begins by presenting a logical reductio against the transmigrationists. He imagines two temperaments arising simultaneously and shows that on their own principles, this leads to impossible consequences. He then anticipates their objection that two equal temperaments cannot occur, and refutes it with two compelling arguments. This passage is a model of dialectical reasoning in kalam.

Guided Path
1
Understand the initial scenario
Read the first part of the passage where two temperaments occur simultaneously. Follow how the author derives the necessity of two souls and the equal relation leading to absurdity.
The key step is recognizing that if each soul relates equally to both temperaments, each soul must attach to both bodies.
2
Identify the absurd consequences
The author concludes two impossibilities: two souls in one body, and one soul in two bodies. Notice that these are mutually exclusive but both follow from the same assumption.
3
Analyze the objection and first response
The transmigrationist denies that two equal temperaments can occur. The author's first response shows the argument does not require equality – because all souls are identical, any soul can attach to any temperament.
This is a powerful move that undermines the objection's basis.
4
Examine the second response
The author argues that equal temperaments are possible because the conditions for a temperament can recur, making simultaneous identical temperaments possible. This confirms the initial reductio.
The argument uses the principle that what is possible can occur.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا حدث مزاجان دفعة واحدة وجب أن يحدث نفسان متعلقتان بهما. ثم نسبة كل واحد من ذينك المزاجين إلى تينك النفسين على السوية، فلم يكن تعلق إحدى النفسين بأحد المزاجين أولى من العكس. فيلزم تعلق كل واحدة من النفسين بكل واحد من البدنين، وذلك يوجب القول بحصول النفسين في البدن الواحد، وحصول النفس الواحدة في البدنين. فثبت أن ما ألزموه من المحال فضعف لازم عليهم. فإن قالوا: هذا بناء على أنه يمكن حدوث مزاجين متساويين دفعة واحدة، وهو ممنوع. قلنا: الجواب عنه من وجهين: الأول: إن هذا الإلزام لا يتوقف على بيان أن المزاجين الحادثين في الوقت الواحد مثلان أو مختلفان. وذلك لأن هذا الدليل مفرع على أن النفوس الناطقة متماثلة، وحكم الشيء حكم مثله. فكل مزاج يقبل نفسا، وجب أن يكون قابلاً لسائر النفوس. وحينئذ يعود الإلزام، سواء قلنا: إن تلك الأمزجة متماثلة أو مختلفة معينة. الثاني: إن المزاج المخصوص إنما حدث بناء على شرطين: أحدهما: حصول أجزاء مخصوصة من العناصر الأربعة، مقدرة بمقادير [؟]. والثاني: امتزاج تلك الأشياء واختلاطها على وجه خاص مدة معينة. وإذا عرفت هذا فنقول: حصول أجزاء أخرى من العناصر الأربعة مقدرة بالمقادير المعينة ومختلطة على ذلك الوجه المعين: ممكن. والموقوف على الممكن ممكن. فوجب القطع بأنه يمكن حدوث مزاجين متساويين في وقت واحد. وهو المطلوب.
So if two temperaments (mizajan) occur simultaneously, two souls (nafsan) must occur attached to them. Then the relation of each of those two temperaments to those two souls is equal, so the attachment of one soul to one temperament is not more likely than the opposite. Thus it necessitates the attachment of each of the two souls to each of the two bodies, and that necessitates saying that two souls exist in one body, and one soul exists in two bodies. So it is established that what they [the transmigrationists] have necessitated of absurdity is [itself] a weakness necessary upon them. If they say: this is based on the possibility of two equal temperaments occurring simultaneously, and that is denied. We say: the answer to it is from two aspects. The first: this necessitation does not depend on showing that the two temperaments occurring at the same time are similar or different. That is because this proof is based on the fact that rational souls are similar, and the ruling of a thing is the ruling of its like. So every temperament that accepts a soul, it must be capable of accepting all souls. And at that point the necessitation returns, whether we say that those temperaments are similar or specifically different. The second: the specific temperament only occurs based on two conditions: one of them: the occurrence of specific parts of the four elements, measured by specific measures [؟]; and the second: the mixing and blending of those things in a specific manner for a specific duration. And if you understand this, we say: the occurrence of other parts of the four elements measured by those specific measures and mixed in that specific manner is possible. And that which depends on the possible is possible. So it is necessary to decide that it is possible for two equal temperaments to occur at one time. And that is what was required.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage presents the first argument against the doctrine of transmigration of souls (tanasukh). The argument is structured as a reductio ad absurdum. The author begins by positing a scenario: if two temperaments (mizajan) come into existence simultaneously, then according to the transmigrationists' view that each temperament receives a soul, two souls must attach to them. Since the temperaments are equally related to the souls, there is no reason for one soul to attach to one temperament rather than the other. This leads to the absurd consequence that each soul attaches to both bodies, implying either two souls in one body or one soul in two bodies—both impossible. The author then anticipates an objection: the transmigrationists might deny that two equal temperaments can occur simultaneously. The author responds with two arguments. First, the reductio does not depend on the equality of the temperaments; even if temperaments differ, the same consequence follows because all rational souls are identical in essence. If one temperament can accept one soul, it can accept any soul, so the absurdity remains. Second, the author argues that the occurrence of two equal temperaments is possible. Since a specific temperament depends on specific quantities and mixing of elements, and since such conditions can recur, it is possible for two identical temperaments to arise at the same time. Thus, the objection is refuted.

نفس
مزاج
تماثل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument against transmigration only works if the two simultaneous temperaments are exactly equal.
Correction: The author shows that even if the temperaments are different, the same absurdity follows because rational souls are homogeneous and every temperament that can accept one soul can accept any soul.

Checkpoint
What is the absurd consequence that the author derives from the assumption that two temperaments occur simultaneously?
A) Two souls cannot coexist in one body.
B) Each soul attaches to both bodies, leading to either two souls in one body or one soul in two bodies.
C) The number of souls must equal the number of bodies.
D) Temperaments cannot be equal.

Key Takeaway
The transmigrationist view leads to logical absurdities regardless of whether the supposed temperaments are equal or different, as the homogeneity of souls ensures that every temperament is receptive to every soul.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt that your soul is uniquely yours, or that you share a spiritual connection with another person in a way that the argument calls 'one soul in two bodies'? How does the author's denial of such a possibility challenge your assumptions about relationships?
?
If all rational souls are identical in essence, what does that mean for how you view other people's souls compared to your own? Are you truly distinct from others in your deepest identity, or are you part of a larger reality?
?
The transmigrationist view is shown to be logically absurd. Does your own understanding of the afterlife rely on any unexamined assumptions? How does this argument strengthen your trust in the Islamic position of resurrection?

The Second Argument Against Transmigration: No Idleness and the Objection
The second argument against tanasukh using the no-idleness principle, followed by the first aspect of the transmigrationist objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical structure of the second argument against transmigration (tanasukh) based on the principle that nature avoids idleness, and the first part of the objection raised against it.

Core Idea
Transmigration fails because nature abhors idle souls, but the objection argues that this principle backfires, leaving infant souls eternally idle.

This passage presents a key argument against transmigration (tanasukh) that relies on the principle that nature avoids idleness. After explaining the argument, the author introduces an objection from the transmigrationists, who claim that the anti-transmigration position itself leads to absurdities. The lesson focuses on understanding the logical structure of the argument and the beginning of the critical response.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Pay attention to the initial dichotomy: either souls remain idle or they immediately attach to new bodies.
The argument uses a reductio ad absurdum.
2
Identify the two horns
The argument first shows that the horn of idleness is false because nature has no idleness. Then it shows that the other horn implies equal numbers of births and deaths, which is contradicted by historical events like floods.
3
Examine the objection's first aspect
The transmigrationists attack the principle of no idleness. They cite Themistius and argue that the anti-transmigration position itself accepts idle souls (infants, fetuses, mentally deficient), which is worse than their own view.
Note how the objection tries to show inconsistency.
4
Reflect on the author's response
The passage ends with the author's judgment that this objection is extremely far-fetched. Consider why the author might say that.
The answer is not given in this passage; you may need to think critically.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية لمنكري التناسخ: قالوا: النفوس المفارقة لأبدانها. إما أن عليها: أن تبقى مجردة مدة، من غير أن تكن متعلقة بأبدان أخرى، وإما أن لا يصح ذلك. والأول باطل. لأنها تكون فيما بين الوقتين: معطلة ولا معطل في الطبيعة. والثاني يوجب أن يكون عدد الهالكين مساوياً لعدد الكائنين، حتى يقال: إنه عندما فسد بدن، وفارقته نفسه. ففي تلك الحالة يكون قد استعد بدن آخر لتتعلق به تلك النفس. ومعلوم أنه ليس الأمر كذلك، فإن في الطوفانات العامة التي عندها ينقطع النسل، نعلم أن عدد المالكين أكثر من عدد الكاثنين. والاعتراض على هذا الكلام من وجهين: الأول: إن قولكم: لا معطل في الطبيعة: كلام لم يذكروا في تقريره شبهة. فضلا عن حجة. ثم إنه منقوض على أصولكم بأشياء أولها: إن ثامسطوس زعم: أن النفوس الباقية بعد مفارقة الأبدان النفوس الفاضلة الكاملة، وأما نفوس الأطفال والجهال فإنها تفسد، وإلا لبقيت معطلة، ولا معطل في الطبيعة. ثم إنكم ما التفتم إلى هذا الكلام، وما أقمتم له وزناً. وحكمتم ببقاء نفوس الأجنة والأطفال والمعتوهين، أبد الآباد ودهر الداهرين: معطلة، خالية عن الفعل والانفعال. ومعلوم: أن ذلك التعطيل: أكمل لأن هذه النفوس التناسخية، قد حصل لها شيء كثير من العلوم والأخلاق، فهي منتفعة بتلك الصفات. ثم إنها عن قريب تتعلق بأبدان أخرى، وتتخلص عن تلك المعطلة. وأما نفوس الأطفال فليس معها شيء من العقائد والأخلاق، فتبقى عطلتها أبداً سرمداً. ثم إنكم جوزتم، ومنعتم من ذلك. وهذا في غاية البعد.
The second proof of those who deny transmigration: They said: The souls that separate from their bodies: either it is necessary for them to remain abstract for a period, without being attached to other bodies, or that is not possible. The first is false because they would be, in the interval, idle (muʿaṭṭala), and there is no idleness (muʿaṭṭal) in nature. The second necessitates that the number of the dying (hālikīn) be equal to the number of the coming into being (kāʾinīn), so that it is said: when a body corrupts and its soul separates from it, then at that moment another body has become prepared for that soul to attach to it. But it is known that the matter is not so, for in general floods when reproduction ceases, we know that the number of the dead (mālikīn) is greater than the number of the coming into being (kāthinīn). The objection to this statement is from two aspects: The first: your statement 'there is no idleness in nature' is a statement whose verification they have not mentioned even a suspicion, let alone a proof. Then it is refuted upon your principles by things, the first of which: Themistius claimed that the souls remaining after separation from bodies are the excellent and perfect souls, while the souls of children and the ignorant perish, otherwise they would remain idle, and there is no idleness in nature. Then you paid no attention to this statement, and you did not give it any weight. And you judged the permanence of the souls of fetuses, children, and the mentally deficient forever and ever: idle, free from action and passion. And it is known that that idleness is more perfect because these transmigrationist souls have acquired much knowledge and character, so they benefit from those qualities. Then soon they attach to other bodies and escape that idleness. But the souls of children have no beliefs or character with them, so their idleness remains eternal. Then you permitted and forbade that. And this is extremely far-fetched.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage presents the second argument against transmigration (tanasukh) and then introduces an objection. The argument begins with a dichotomy: after separation from the body, souls must either remain abstract without attaching to another body, or they must attach to another body immediately. The first option is deemed false because it would leave souls idle for a period, and according to a principle, there is no idleness (lā muʿaṭṭal) in nature. The second option implies that the number of souls dying must equal the number of souls being born so that every body is immediately occupied. However, historical evidence (e.g., great floods where reproduction ceases) shows that the number of the dead exceeds the number of the newly born, contradicting the claim. The author then presents an objection from the transmigrationists against this argument. The objection has two aspects. The first aspect attacks the principle of no idleness: the opponents claim that this principle is unsubstantiated, and moreover, it is contradicted by the transmigrationists' own acceptance of idle souls, such as those of fetuses, children, and the mentally deficient, whom they believe remain idle forever. Themistius is cited as holding that only perfect souls survive, while the imperfect perish—otherwise they would be idle. The transmigrationists, however, hold that all souls survive, including those of infants, leading to eternal idleness for them, which is more problematic than their own view where souls benefit from knowledge before rebirth. This objection criticizes the consistency of the anti-transmigration stance. The passage ends with the remark that this objection is extremely far-fetched, but the author does not provide a counter-answer within this excerpt.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The 'no idleness in nature' principle is a universally accepted axiom that cannot be questioned.
Correction: The objection shows that the principle is contested and its application leads to contradictions: anti-transmigrationists themselves admit idle souls (infants, etc.), so the principle is either false or not consistently applied.

Checkpoint

D) The impossibility of equal temperaments.

Key Takeaway
The second argument against tanasukh uses the dilemma of idle souls versus immediate reattachment, but the transmigrationist objection challenges the no-idleness principle by pointing to the eternal idleness of infant souls—a point the author dismisses as far-fetched without further justification in this excerpt.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

If you were to die tonight, what would your soul carry with it to the next life? Would it be like the souls of children who have no beliefs or character, left idle forever, or would it have the knowledge and moral qualities that benefit it in the afterlife? This lesson forces you to ask: what are you accumulating right now that will survive death?
?
The transmigrationist objection says leaving infant souls eternally idle is unjust. Do you truly believe that God’s mercy and justice are fully expressed in the fate of those who die young? If so, how does the author's dismissal of this objection as 'extremely far-fetched' sit with your conscience? What does your answer reveal about your trust in divine wisdom?
?
The principle 'no idleness in nature' condemns spiritual idleness as unnatural. What parts of your spiritual life have become idle—prayer without presence, charity without sacrifice, knowledge without action? Today, what specific step will you take to reattach your soul to a purpose that will not be left idle at death?

The Two Major Views on the Soul
Classification of two views on the soul and emphasis on their importance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two competing views on the soul held by scholars and why this issue is critically important.

Core Idea
The soul is either a body with temperament or a self-subsisting substance.

This lesson opens a new chapter on the identity of the person after death. The author declares that no issue is more important for a rational person than this one. He then presents the two fundamental schools of thought on the soul: the materialist view and the spiritualist view. This classification is essential for understanding debates on resurrection.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening importance statement
Notice how the author emphasizes that this is the most important issue for a rational person. This sets the tone for the entire discussion.
2
Identify the two views
The passage presents two views: first, the soul is a specific body with a specific temperament; second, it is a self-subsisting substance distinct from the body.
The second view includes two possible definitions: a non-elemental body or a non-corporeal substance.
3
Reflect on the difference
Contrast the materialist view (soul as body) with the spiritualist view (soul as independent substance). Consider how each view affects the possibility of resurrection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل التاسع في بيان أن الشخص بالنية بعد موت البدن   
اعلم : أنك لا ترى في الدنيا مسألة أهم للعاقل من هذه المسألة ، فوجب على كل من عنده شيء من العقل، أن يكون عظيم الاهتمام بمعرفتها . فنقول أهل العلم لهم في النفس مذهبان :  
أحدهما : إنها عبارة عن جسم مخصوص ، موصوف بمزاج مخصوص . والثاني : إنها جوهر قائم بذاته، مغاير لهذا البدن ، ولجميع أجزائه سواء قلنا: إنه جسم مخالف للأجسام العنصرية البسيطة أو المركبة، أو قلنا: إنه جوهر ليس بجسم ولا يجسماني .  
أما القائلون بالقول الأول . فهم فريقان :  
أحدهما : أهل البحث والنظر  
وثانيهما : أهل التقليد والأثر. أما أهل البحث والنظر فالجمهور منهم اتفقوا على أن النفس بهذا التفسير يمتنع نقلها بعد موت البدن ، بناء على أن القول بالبعث والقيامة غير ممكن. وذلك لأنه بعد الموت قد فني هذا المزاج ، وبطل هذا التركيب . والمعلوم يمتنع عوده بعينه
The Ninth Chapter: On Explaining that the Person (remains) with Intention after the Death of the Body  
Know that you see in the world no issue more important for the rational person than this issue. So it is incumbent upon everyone who has some intellect to be greatly concerned with knowing it. We say: The people of knowledge have two schools of thought (madhhabān) regarding the soul:  
One of them: That it is a specific body, described with a specific temperament (mizāj).  
And the second: That it is a self-subsisting substance (jawhar qā'im bi-dhātihī), distinct from this body and from all its parts, whether we say that it is a body contrary to elemental bodies (al-ajsām al-ʿunṣuriyya), simple or compound, or we say that it is a substance that is neither a body nor corporeal (jismānī).  
As for those who hold the first statement, they are two groups:  
One of them: The people of investigation and reflection (ahl al-baḥth wa al-naẓar),  
And the second: The people of tradition and received reports (ahl al-taqlīd wa al-athar).  
As for the people of investigation and reflection, the majority of them agreed that the soul, by this interpretation, cannot be transferred after the death of the body, based on the fact that the statement of resurrection (al-baʿth) and the Last Day (al-qiyāma) is not possible. That is because after death this temperament has perished and this composition (tarkīb) has become invalid. And what has ceased to exist cannot return exactly as it was.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage begins a new chapter on the identity of the person after death. The author asserts that this is the most important issue for a rational person, emphasizing its gravity. He then classifies two main views on the soul: the first view holds that the soul is a specific body characterized by a specific temperament (mizāj). The second view holds that the soul is a self-subsisting substance (jawhar qā'im bi-dhātihī), distinct from the body and its parts, and it may be either a non-elemental body or a non-corporeal substance. The author then subdivides the proponents of the first view into two groups: the people of investigation and reflection (ahl al-baḥth wa al-naẓar) and the people of tradition and received reports (ahl al-taqlīd wa al-athar). He explains that the majority of the investigators agree that the soul, according to the first interpretation (as a body with temperament), cannot be transferred after death, because the temperament and composition are destroyed at death and cannot be exactly reconstituted. Therefore, they deny the possibility of resurrection and the Last Day.

Key Terms
نفس (nafs)
بدن (badan)
مزاج (mizāj)
جوهر قائم بذاته (jawhar qā'im bi-dhātihī)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All scholars agree on the nature of the soul.
Correction: The author presents two distinct views: the soul as a material body with temperament, or as a self-subsisting substance distinct from the body.

Checkpoint

C) Soul as spirit and soul as mind
D) Soul as eternal and soul as created

Key Takeaway
There are two major views on the soul: one materialist (body with temperament) and one spiritualist (self-subsisting substance).

?
If your soul is a self-subsisting substance, then your actions are not merely chemical reactions—they shape an eternal reality. Does that truth unsettle you? What specific habit will you change today to honor that reality?

Why Materialists Deny Resurrection
Subdivision of the materialist view and argument against resurrection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the materialist view of the soul leads to the denial of resurrection.

Core Idea
If the soul is only a temporary composition, it cannot be reconstituted after death.

The author now examines the first view more closely, splitting its proponents into two groups: investigators and traditionalists. He explains that most investigators agree that if the soul is merely a body with a specific temperament, then resurrection is impossible because the composition is destroyed at death and cannot return exactly as it was. This argument highlights the stakes of the debate on the soul's nature.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two groups within the first view
The people of investigation and reflection, and the people of tradition and reports.
2
Understand the majority opinion of the investigators
Most investigators agreed that the soul (as a body with temperament) cannot be transferred after death.
3
Grasp the reasoning
After death, the temperament perishes and the composition becomes invalid. What has ceased to exist cannot return exactly as it was, so resurrection is impossible.

The Ninth Chapter: On Explaining that the Person (remains) with Intention after the Death of the Body  
Know that you see in the world no issue more important for the rational person than this issue. So it is incumbent upon everyone who has some intellect to be greatly concerned with knowing it. We say: The people of knowledge have two schools of thought (madhhabān) regarding the soul:  
One of them: That it is a specific body, described with a specific temperament (mizāj).  
And the second: That it is a self-subsisting substance (jawhar qā'im bi-dhātihī), distinct from this body and from all its parts, whether we say that it is a body contrary to elemental bodies (al-ajsām al-ʿunṣuriyya), simple or compound, or we say that it is a substance that is neither a body nor corporeal (jismānī).  
As for those who hold the first statement, they are two groups:  
One of them: The people of investigation and reflection (ahl al-baḥth wa al-naẓar),  
And the second: The people of tradition and received reports (ahl al-taqlīd wa al-athar).  
As for the people of investigation and reflection, the majority of them agreed that the soul, by this interpretation, cannot be transferred after the death of the body, based on the fact that the statement of resurrection (al-baʿth) and the Last Day (al-qiyāma) is not possible. That is because after death this temperament has perished and this composition (tarkīb) has become invalid. And what has ceased to exist cannot return exactly as it was.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage begins a new chapter on the identity of the person after death. The author asserts that this is the most important issue for a rational person, emphasizing its gravity. He then classifies two main views on the soul: the first view holds that the soul is a specific body characterized by a specific temperament (mizāj). The second view holds that the soul is a self-subsisting substance (jawhar qā'im bi-dhātihī), distinct from the body and its parts, and it may be either a non-elemental body or a non-corporeal substance. The author then subdivides the proponents of the first view into two groups: the people of investigation and reflection (ahl al-baḥth wa al-naẓar) and the people of tradition and received reports (ahl al-taqlīd wa al-athar). He explains that the majority of the investigators agree that the soul, according to the first interpretation (as a body with temperament), cannot be transferred after death, because the temperament and composition are destroyed at death and cannot be exactly reconstituted. Therefore, they deny the possibility of resurrection and the Last Day.

Key Terms
بعث (baʿth)
قيامة (qiyāma)
مزاج (mizāj)
تركيب (tarkīb)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The materialist view can still accept resurrection if God recreates the body.
Correction: The author states that for those holding the materialist view, the majority of investigators agree that resurrection is impossible because the exact composition cannot return.

Checkpoint
According to the text, why do materialist investigators deny resurrection?
A) Because the soul is immortal
B) Because the temperament and composition are destroyed and cannot return exactly
C) Because they follow tradition
D) Because they believe in reincarnation

Key Takeaway
If the soul is merely a temporary composition, its destruction at death makes resurrection impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that death is the end of your existence, how would you live differently? What would you prioritize? Now contrast that with the Islamic belief in resurrection. Is your current life aligned with that belief?
?
The materialists claim that the composition cannot return exactly as it was. Do you trust that Allah can recreate you perfectly? What doubts or fears about your own resurrection do you need to address right now?
?
This passage shows that some base their rejection of resurrection on reasoning. Have you ever let your own reasoning weaken your certainty in the unseen matters of the Hereafter? What step will you take today to strengthen your faith in the resurrection beyond mere intellectual acceptance?
