The Two Views on the Soul and Their Implications for Resurrection
Enumeration of two opinions on the soul and their subgroups.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two main scholarly opinions on the nature of the soul and why the physicalist view leads to denying resurrection.

Core Idea
The soul's nature determines whether resurrection is possible.

The author begins by emphasizing that understanding the soul is the most important intellectual task. He outlines the two major schools: one sees the soul as a specific body with a mixture, the other as an independent substance. This classification sets the stage for the debate on bodily resurrection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once for overall meaning. Then read the translation to grasp the author's flow.
Pay attention to the author's strong opening about importance.
2
Identify the two opinions on the soul
Find where the author states the two schools of thought. Notice how he defines each one.
The first opinion defines the soul as a body with a specific mixture; the second as a self-subsisting substance distinct from the body.
3
Understand the rationalist consequence
See how the rationalist investigators, who hold the first opinion, conclude that the soul cannot survive death and therefore resurrection is impossible.
4
Contrast the traditionalist position
Observe that the traditionalists accept both physicalism and resurrection without considering their compatibility.
This sets up the need for reconciliation attempts in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل التاسع في بيان أن النفس بعد موت البدن. اعلم أنك لا ترى في الدنيا مسألة أهم للعاقل من هذه المسألة، فوجب على كل من عنده شيء من العقل أن يكون عظيم الاهتمام بمعرفتها. فنقول: أهل العلم لهم في النفس مذهبان: أحدهما: إنها عبارة عن جسم مخصوص، موصوف بمزاج مخصوص. والثاني: إنها جوهر قائم بذاته، مغاير لهذا البدن، ولجميع أجزائه سواء قلنا: إنه جسم مخالف للأجسام العنصرية البسيطة أو المركبة، أو قلنا: إنه جوهر ليس بجسم ولا جسماني. أما القائلون بالقول الأول فهم فريقان: أحدهما: أهل البحث والنظر، وثانيهما: أهل التقليد والأثر. أما أهل البحث والنظر فالجمهور منهم اتفقوا على أن النفس بهذا التفسير يمتنع بقاؤها بعد موت البدن، بناء على أن القول بالبعث والقيامة غير ممكن. وذلك لأنه بعد الموت قد فني هذا المزاج، وبطل هذا التركيب، والمعلوم يمتنع عوده بعينه. وأما أهل التقليد والأثر فهم قد اعتقدوا أنه لا حقيقة للإنسان إلا هذا الهيكل، وسمعوا من الأنبياء والعلماء إثبات القول بالبعث والقيامة، فاعتقدوا كلا القولين ولم تصل خواطرهم إلى أن الجمع بين هذين القولين هل هو ممكن لا. ثم إن جماعة من المتكلمين لما أرادوا أن يجمعوا بين هذين القولين ذكروا فيه طريقين: الأول: قال بعضهم: إن إعادة المعدوم بعينه جائز. والثاني: قال آخرون: إنه محال، إلا أنه إذا مات الإنسان فإنه لا تفنى تلك الأجزاء أو تلك الذوات، وإنما يفنى المزاج والصفات. فإذا أعيد التركيب والمزاج إلى تلك الأجزاء، كان الإنسان العائد عين الإنسان الذي كان موجودا في الدنيا. وهذا في غاية البعد، لأنا نقول: الإنسان المعين إما أن يكون عبارة عن تلك الأجزاء كيف كانت، أو عينها بشرط كونها موصوفة بصفات مخصوصة. والأول باطل، لأن تلك الأجزاء حال ما كانت خالية عن العلم والحياة والقدرة والمزاج والتأليف، كانت موجودة مع أن هذا الإنسان ما كان موجودا. فإذا مات هذا الإنسان وزالت هذه الصفات، فإن تلك الأجزاء تكون باقية مع أن ذلك الإنسان قد لا يكون باقيا. وهذا يدل على أن هذا الإنسان ليس عبارة عن تلك الأجزاء كيف كانت، بل إن كان ولا بد فالإنسان المعين عبارة عن تلك الأجزاء المخصوصة بشرط قيام صفات مخصوصة بها. فإذا عدمت تلك الصفات، فقد عدم أحد الأجزاء المقومة لماهية ذلك الإنسان المعين، وحينئذ يحصل الجزم بأن ذلك الإنسان قد عدم وفني. ثم عند هذا نقول: إن كانت إعادة المعدوم ممكنة، فلا حاجة إلى القول ببقاء تلك الذوات، وإن كانت غير ممكنة لم يكن القول ببقاء تلك الذوات كافيا في القول بصحة عود ذلك الإنسان بعينه.
Chapter Nine: An exposition that the soul after the death of the body. Know that you do not see in the world a matter more important for the rational person than this matter, so it is obligatory upon everyone who has any intellect to have great concern for knowing it. We say: The people of knowledge have two schools of thought concerning the soul: One of them: That it is an expression of a specific body, described with a specific mixture. The second: That it is a self-subsisting substance, distinct from this body, and from all its parts, whether we say that it is a body different from the elemental bodies, simple or compound, or we say that it is a substance that is neither a body nor corporeal. As for those who hold the first opinion, they are two groups: One of them: The people of investigation and reflection. The second: The people of tradition and transmitted reports. As for the people of investigation and reflection, the majority of them agreed that the soul according to this interpretation is impossible to survive after the death of the body, based on the claim that the belief in resurrection and the Last Day is impossible. That is because after death this mixture has perished, and this composition has become null, and it is known that its exact return is impossible. As for the people of tradition and transmitted reports, they believed that there is no reality for man except this structure, and they heard from the prophets and scholars the affirmation of the belief in resurrection and the Last Day, so they believed both statements, and their thoughts did not reach whether the combination of these two statements is possible or not. Then when a group of theologians (mutakallimun) wanted to combine these two statements, they mentioned two methods: First: Some of them said: The re-creation of the exact non-existent is permissible. Second: Others said: It is impossible, except that when a man dies, those parts or those essences do not perish, only the mixture and attributes perish. So if the composition and mixture are restored to those parts, the returning man would be the exact man who existed in the world. And this is extremely far-fetched, for we say: The specific man is either an expression of those parts however they are, or the exact parts with the condition that they are described with specific attributes. The first is false, because those parts when they were devoid of knowledge, life, power, mixture, and composition existed while this man did not exist. So when this man dies and these attributes cease, those parts remain while that man may not remain. And this indicates that this man is not an expression of those parts however they are, but if it must be, then the specific man is an expression of those specific parts with the condition that specific attributes subsist in them. So when those attributes cease, then one of the constitutive parts of the essence of that specific man has ceased, and then there is certainty that that man has ceased and perished. Then upon this we say: If the re-creation of the exact non-existent is possible, then there is no need for the claim of the survival of those essences, and if it is not possible, then the claim of the survival of those essences is not sufficient for the claim of the validity of the return of that exact man.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage is a complex argument about the nature of the soul (nafs) and the possibility of bodily resurrection after death. The author begins by stressing the supreme importance of this question for any rational person. He then presents two fundamental opinions among scholars regarding the soul: first, that it is a specific body with a specific mixture (mizaj); second, that it is a self-subsisting substance (jawhar qā'im bi-dhātihī) distinct from the body and its parts, whether considered as a different kind of body or as a non-corporeal substance. He then focuses on the first opinion (soul as body) and divides its proponents into two groups: the rationalist investigators (ahl al-baḥth wa al-nazar) and the traditionalists (ahl al-taqlīd wa al-athar). The rationalists, he explains, concluded from this identification of soul with body that the soul cannot survive bodily death, and therefore resurrection is impossible—since after death the specific mixture and composition are gone and cannot return identically. The traditionalists, on the other hand, held that man is only this physical structure, yet they heard from prophets and scholars the affirmation of resurrection and believed both (the physicalist view and resurrection) without examining whether they are compatible. The author then reports that later theologians (mutakallimūn) attempted to reconcile these two positions by two methods: the first method asserts that God can recreate the exact non-existent (i'ādat al-ma'dūm bi-'aynihi) is possible; the second method denies that possibility but claims that the material parts (or essences) of the person do not perish at death—only the mixture and attributes perish—so that if the composition and mixture are restored to those same parts, the returning person would be identical to the original person. The author then refutes the second method as extremely far-fetched. He presents a logical argument: the specific individual human (al-insān al-mu'ayyan) must be either the parts considered absolutely (without conditions) or the parts considered with the condition of possessing specific attributes (like knowledge, life, power, mixture, composition). The first option is false because those parts can exist without those attributes (e.g., before the person's life), yet the individual human did not exist then. Therefore, the individual human is essentially the parts plus those specific attributes. When death occurs and those attributes cease, one of the constitutive elements (al-ajzā' al-muqawwima) of that human's essence ceases, so the human has perished. Consequently, if re-creation of the exact non-existent is possible, there is no need to posit the survival of the essences; if it is not possible, then merely preserving the material parts does not guarantee the return of the identical person. Hence, the second reconciliation method fails.

Key Terms
النفس (nafs)
الجسم (jism)
المزاج (mizaj)
الجوهر (jawhar)
البعث (ba'th)
القيامة (qiyāma)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that all physicalists necessarily deny resurrection, but the traditionalists accept both without logical reconciliation.
Correction: The author shows that physicalists are divided: rationalists deny resurrection, traditionalists accept it without consistency.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what conclusion do the rationalist investigators (ahl al-baḥth wa al-nazar) draw from defining the soul as a specific body with a specific mixture?
A) The soul can survive death through reincarnation.
B) The soul is immortal and therefore resurrection is certain.
C) The soul cannot survive death, so resurrection is impossible.
D) The soul is a self-subsisting substance.

Key Takeaway
The physicalist view of the soul, when taken to its logical conclusion, denies the possibility of bodily resurrection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about your own death and what happens to you, do you truly investigate the nature of your soul, or do you simply rely on inherited beliefs? What would change if you took this question as seriously as the author insists?
?
The traditionalists accepted both statements without thinking about compatibility. In what areas of your own aqeedah might you be doing the same? What would it take for you to honestly examine those tensions?
?
If the rationalists are wrong about the soul being merely a mixture, what does that mean for your confidence in purely rational arguments about the unseen? Are you willing to reconsider foundational assumptions about your own identity based on revelation?

Reconciling Physicalism with Resurrection: A Refutation
Refutation of a reconciliation attempt for resurrection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two theological attempts to reconcile physicalism with resurrection and why the author finds the second attempt insufficient.

Core Idea
Preserving the material parts does not guarantee the same person returns.

The author presents two methods proposed by theologians to combine the belief that the soul is merely a body with the belief in resurrection. He then refutes the second method by arguing that the individual person is defined by specific attributes, not just material parts, so death destroys the person.

Guided Path
1
Read the reconciliation attempts
Find the two methods theologians used to try to make physicalism and resurrection compatible.
First method: re-creation of the non-existent is possible. Second method: parts survive, only mixture perishes.
2
Understand the refutation target
The author focuses on refuting the second method. Note how he sets up the argument.
3
Analyze the logical argument
The author examines whether the individual human is the parts absolutely or the parts with specific attributes. Follow his reasoning to see why the second method fails.
4
Conclude the lesson
The author concludes that either re-creation of the non-existent is possible (no need for parts) or it is not (parts insufficient). Either way, the second method is ineffective.

Commentary
This passage is a complex argument about the nature of the soul (nafs) and the possibility of bodily resurrection after death. The author begins by stressing the supreme importance of this question for any rational person. He then presents two fundamental opinions among scholars regarding the soul: first, that it is a specific body with a specific mixture (mizaj); second, that it is a self-subsisting substance (jawhar qā'im bi-dhātihī) distinct from the body and its parts, whether considered as a different kind of body or as a non-corporeal substance. Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that as long as the material parts of a person survive, God can reassemble them to make the same person.
Correction: The author shows that the person is defined by specific attributes, not just material parts. The loss of attributes means the person is gone, and mere reassembly of parts does not restore identity.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why does the second reconciliation method (parts survive, attributes perish) fail to guarantee the return of the identical person?
A) Because it is impossible to restore the exact mixture and composition.
B) Because the specific attributes (like knowledge and life) are constitutive of the individual, so their loss means the person has perished.
C) Because the material parts also perish at death.
D) Because the first method already proved re-creation is possible.

Key Takeaway
The identity of a person depends on both material parts and specific attributes; the loss of attributes at death destroys the person, making mere material continuity insufficient for resurrection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your identity is not merely your body but the specific attributes Allah has given you (knowledge, life, faith), then which of those attributes are you most actively preserving and strengthening? Will they accompany you to the grave?
?
The author insists that when attributes like knowledge and life cease, 'one of the constitutive parts of the essence' is lost. What does that say about your current attachment to your physical existence? Are you living as if your essence is tied to this world?
?
If the same physical parts do not guarantee the same person returns at resurrection, then what is the real basis of your hope for reunion with loved ones in the afterlife? Do you trust in Allah's power to re-create you as the same person despite your dissolution?

Introduction to the Soul's Survival After Death
Introduces the two views on human nature and the plan to argue for soul's survival.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two competing views on human nature and how the author grounds the soul's survival on the prior proof of its simplicity.

Core Idea
The soul's survival is a conclusion built on the foundation that the soul is a simple substance.

This lesson introduces one of the most important topics in Islamic theology: the survival of the soul after death. The author, Imam al-Razi, begins by summarizing two opposing views on what constitutes a human being. He then clarifies that his own position—that the soul is a simple substance distinct from the body—has already been established, and the claim of survival follows logically from it. Finally, he announces his intention to present all possible arguments, both demonstrative and persuasive, to support this doctrine.

Guided Path
1
Understand the two views on human nature
Read the passage carefully and identify the two definitions of 'man' that are presented: one as a body with specific temperament, the other as a simple substance distinct from the body.
The first view reduces man to the physical body, while the second sees a separate spiritual essence.
2
Recognize the author's position
Notice that the author aligns with the second view (soul as simple substance) and notes that all who hold this view agree on the soul's survival.
This sets the stage for the rest of the discussion.
3
Trace the logical grounding
The author states that the soul's survival is 'branched upon' (مفرعاً) the principle that the soul is a simple substance. Understand that this survival is not just a belief but a necessary conclusion from prior proof.
This is a crucial hermeneutical move: the survival is a derived, not a primary, claim.
4
Note the comprehensive approach
The author commits to covering all possible arguments—both demonstrative (برهانية) and persuasive (إقناعية)—due to the importance of the issue.
This shows the thoroughness of the treatment to come.

The author reminds us that they have already proven that the soul is a simple substance, so the claim of its survival is based on that principle. Then the author states the importance of this issue and their plan to present all possible arguments, both demonstrative and persuasive.

The Soul's Independence from the Body Claims Its Survival
Argues that the soul's independence from the body entails its survival.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first proof for the soul's survival after death: that the soul's independence from the body as a simple substance means its death does not follow from the body's death.

Core Idea
The soul is not in the body; it only acts through it, like a person in a house.

This lesson presents the first of several proofs for the survival of the soul after death. The author, al-Isfahani, builds on the previously established nature of the soul as a simple substance that is neither a body nor inside a body. He argues that the soul's relation to the body is merely operational—like a person dwelling in a house—so the body's ruin does not necessitate the soul's annihilation. The passage also addresses the source of doubt, which arises from mistakenly imagining the soul as in-dwelling.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Pay attention to the flow: premise, explanation, analogy, rebuttal.
The passage is a single continuous argument.
2
Identify the three components of the proof
First, locate the premise that the rational soul is a simple substance. Second, find the analogy of the person and the house. Third, identify the refutation of the false imagination (wahm).
These components form the backbone of the argument.
3
Reflect on the necessary knowledge claim
The author says the conclusion is a matter of necessary knowledge (daruri). Consider why he thinks this is self-evident once the imagination is corrected.
Necessary knowledge is knowledge that is immediately certain without inference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الأولى على بقاء النفس بعد موت البدن : أن نقول : قد ثبت أن النفس الناطقة : جوهر ليس بجسم ولا في جسم البتة . ويمتنع أن يحصل بينه وبين الأجسام قرب أو بعد أو مناسبة. وليس بينها وبين هذا البدن ، إلا أن هذا البدن محل تصرف ذلك الجوهر في منزل عمله ودار مملكته . كما أن الرجل المعين يكون ساكناً في دار ومتصرفاً فيها ، فإذا خربت تلك الدار وخرجت عن الصلاح والسداد ، لم يلزم موت ذلك المتصرف وبطلانه . وهذا يجري مجرى العلوم الضرورية . والشك والشبهة إنما يتولد بسبب أن الوهم يسبق إلى أن ذلك الشيء حال في هذا البدن ، وساري فيه . فيسبق حينئذ إلى الوهم أنه يجب موتها بموت البدن . وأما إن قدرنا جوهراً مجرداً ليس بينه وبين هذا البدن مناسبة ، لا بالقرب ولا بالبعد ، ولا بوجه من وجوه المناسبة . إلا من وجه واحد ، وهو أن ذلك البدن كان دار مملكة ذلك الجوهر ومحل تصرفه، ثم إنه خربت هذه الدار. فالعلم الضروري حاصل بأن هذا القدر لا يقتضي عدم ذلك الجوهر ولا يغير من أحواله) فهذا لبيان أنه لا يلزم من موت البدن موته حالا.
The first proof for the survival of the soul after the death of the body: We say: It has been established that the rational soul is a substance that is neither a body nor in a body at all. And it is impossible for there to be proximity, distance, or relation between it and bodies. There is no connection between it and this body except that this body is the place of that substance's action, the domain of its work and the kingdom of its dominion. Just as a particular person dwells in a house and acts in it, if that house is ruined and becomes unsound and defective, the death and nullity of that agent does not necessarily follow. This is a matter of necessary knowledge. Doubt and suspicion only arise because the imagination (al-wahm) precedes to [think] that thing is in-dwelling in this body and permeating it. Then it immediately occurs to the imagination that its death is necessitated by the death of the body. But if we assume a simple substance with no relation to this body, not by proximity nor distance nor any aspect of relation, except one aspect: that this body was the kingdom of that substance and the place of its action, then this house is ruined. So necessary knowledge obtains that this amount does not necessitate the non-existence of that substance nor does it change any of its states. So this is to clarify that the death of the body does not necessitate its death at all.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage presents the first proof for the survival of the soul. It begins by restating the established premise: the rational soul is a simple substance, not a body nor residing in a body. Therefore, it cannot have physical relations like proximity or distance with bodies. The only relation is that the body is the domain of the soul's activity. The author gives an analogy: a person living in a house; if the house collapses, the person does not die. So too, the soul does not die with the body. He explains that doubt arises from the imagination that the soul is in-dwelling in the body like a quality in a substance, but once we understand the true nature of the soul as a simple substance with only an operative relation to the body, it becomes necessary knowledge that the body's ruin does not entail the soul's non-existence.

Key Terms

جوهر ليس بجسم ولا في جسم
وهم
علم ضروري
دار مملكة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: the soul is in-dwelling in the body and permeates it, so it must die with the body
Correction: the soul is a simple substance not in the body; its relation is only operational (like a person in a house), so its death does not follow from the body's death.

Key Takeaway

Second Proof: The Soul as Director of the Body
Proves soul's survival by showing circular dependency is impossible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the argument from circular dependency proves that the soul does not die with the body.

Core Idea
If the soul's attributes depended on the body, it would be a vicious circle—impossible and invalid.

This lesson presents the second proof for the soul's survival. The proof is based on the relationship between the soul and the body. The soul directs the body, and its attributes (life, knowledge, power) are necessary for that direction. If those attributes depended on the body's soundness, a circular dependency would result, which is logically impossible. Therefore, the soul must be independent and survive the body's corruption.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof and its analogy
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Notice how the author sets up the dependency and then shows the circularity.
2
Analyze the circular dependency argument
The author argues that if the soul's attributes depended on the body's soundness, then each would depend on the other—a vicious circle. Why is this impossible?
Think about the definition of a vicious circle: it makes explanation impossible.
3
Apply the analogy to God and the world
The author compares the soul-body relationship to God-world relationship. Just as God's attributes do not depend on the world, the soul's attributes do not depend on the body.
This strengthens the conclusion that the soul is independent and survives.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية : لما كان المدبر لهذا الجسد ، والمتولي لإصلاح حاله هو النفس ، ومن المعلوم أن النفس إنما تتولى ذلك بسبب كونها حية عالمة قادرة ، فحينئذ يتوقف صلاح هذا الجسد على كون النفس موصوفة بالحياة والعلم والقدرة . فلو كانت النفس موصوفة بهذه الصفات وهذه الصفات موقوفة على صلاح حال البدن، لزم توقف كل واحد منهما على الآخر وذلك دور . والدور باطل . ومثاله : إنه لما كان حدوث العالم ، وصلاح حاله موقوفاً على كون الإله حياً عالماً قادراً ، امتنع أن يكون حصول هذه الصفات للإله ، موقوفاً على صلاح هذا العالم ، وإلا لزم الدور. فكذا ههنا . فإن النفس لا تعلق لها بالبدن ، إلا تعلقاً شبيهاً بتعلق الإله بالعالم . وذلك من أظهر الدلائل على أن النفس لا تموت بموت البدن ، ولا يفسد شيء من صفاتها بفساد البدن.
The second proof: Since the manager of this body and the one undertaking the reformation of its state is the soul, and it is known that the soul only undertakes that because it is living, knowing, and powerful, then the soundness of this body depends on the soul being described with life, knowledge, and power. So if the soul were described with these attributes and these attributes were dependent on the soundness of the body's state, then each one would depend on the other, and that is a vicious circle (dawr). And a circle is invalid. An example: Since the origination of the world and the soundness of its state depends on the deity being living, knowing, and powerful, it is impossible for the acquisition of these attributes for the deity to depend on the soundness of this world; otherwise a circle would result. So too here. For the soul has no attachment to the body except an attachment similar to the attachment of the deity to the world. And that is among the clearest proofs that the soul does not die with the death of the body, and nothing of its attributes is corrupted by the corruption of the body.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage presents the second proof, based on the relationship between the soul and the body. The soul is the director and caretaker of the body, and it performs this role because it is living, knowing, and powerful. The body's well-being depends on the soul possessing these attributes. If the soul's possession of these attributes depended on the body's well-being, then each would depend on the other, leading to a circular dependency. The author illustrates this with an analogy: God's attributes do not depend on the world, even though the world depends on God. Similarly, the soul's attributes are not dependent on the body. Therefore, the soul and its attributes survive the body's corruption.

Key Terms
مدبر
دور
إله
تعلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The soul's attributes depend on the body's health or soundness.
Correction: If that were the case, it would create a vicious circle because the body's soundness itself depends on the soul's attributes. A circle is logically invalid, so the soul's attributes must be independent of the body.

Checkpoint

B) Contradiction

D) Inconsistency

Key Takeaway
The soul's attributes are independent of the body, as shown by the impossibility of circular dependency, and therefore the soul survives bodily death.

Third Proof: The Soul Does Not Weaken with the Body
Argues soul's independence by observing it does not weaken with body.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the observation that the soul does not weaken with the body proves its independence from the body and its survival after death.

Core Idea
If the soul depended on the body, it would weaken when the body weakens—but it does not.

This lesson presents the third proof from Al-Matalib al-Aliyah, which argues for the soul's independence by observing that the soul does not weaken when the body weakens. The argument is based on a general principle: if something depends on another, the dependent entity must weaken when the source of dependence weakens. Since the soul remains strong despite bodily weakness, it cannot depend on the body and therefore does not die with it. The text is cut off at the end, but the logical conclusion is clear.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze. Then read the translation. Notice the structure: a conditional statement, a principle, and an observation.
The passage is cut off—do not worry about the missing conclusion.
2
Identify the conditional and the observation
The conditional is: if the soul died with the body, it would weaken with it. The observation is: the soul does not weaken with the body. Why is that evidence for independence?
This is the key move in the argument.
3
Understand the underlying principle
The author states that if something is corrupted by the corruption of another, it is in need of that other. Then weakness of the needed causes weakness of the needy. This is a general rule in kalam reasoning.
This principle links dependence to weakness.
4
Apply the principle to the soul and body
If the soul depended on the body, then bodily weakness would cause soul weakness. But the soul does not weaken. Therefore the soul does not depend on the body. The missing conclusion is that the soul does not die with the body.
The argument is sound even though the text cuts off.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثالثة : إنه لو ماتت النفس بموت البدن ، لضعفت بضعف البدن ، وهي لما كانت لا تضعف بضعفه ، وجب أن لا تموت بموت البدن . أما بيان الشرطية : فبالاستقرار الظاهر. فإنه متى وقع الخلل في الأصل ، لزم منه وقوع الخلل في الفرع . ثم نقول : إن الدليل عليه : إن كل شيء يفسد بفساد غيره ، فإنه يكون محتاجاً في ذاته إلى ذلك الغير إذ كل شيء احتاج إلى شيء آخر، فضعف المحتاج إليه، يوجب ضعف المحتاج. إذ لو بقي بحال المحتاج حال نقصان المحتاج إليه، لكانت ...
The third proof: If the soul died with the death of the body, it would weaken with the weakening of the body. But since it does not weaken with its weakening, it must not die with the death of the body. As for the demonstration of the conditional: it is by apparent observation. For whenever a defect occurs in the origin, it necessitates the occurrence of a defect in the branch. Then we say: The evidence for it is: Everything that is corrupted by the corruption of another is in its essence in need of that other. For everything that needs something else, the weakness of the needed necessitates the weakness of the needy. For if the needy remained in its state while the needed is deficient, then it would be ...
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage presents the third proof, which is based on the observation that the soul does not weaken with the body's weakness. If the soul's existence depended on the body, it would necessarily weaken when the body weakens. Since the soul does not weaken (it remains strong even when the body is weak or ill), it cannot be dependent on the body for its existence, and thus does not die with the body. The author begins by stating the conditional and then explains the reasoning: any thing that is corrupted by the corruption of another is inherently dependent on that other; dependence implies that weakness of the dependent follows weakness of the depended-upon. The argument is cut off, but the logical conclusion is that the soul is not dependent and therefore survives.

Key Terms
ضعف (weakness)
أصل (origin)
فرع (branch)
محتاج (needy)
محتاج إليه (needed)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the soul weakens with the body because they observe mental decline in illness.
Correction: The author argues that the soul itself does not weaken; mental decline is due to the body's instrument, not the soul's essence. The soul remains strong even if it cannot act through a weak body.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The observation that the soul does not weaken with the body proves it is independent and does not die with the body.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The Fifth Proof: The Soul Does Not Become Ill with the Body
Ar-Razi presents a causal proof that the soul does not die with the body, based on its not falling ill.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ar-Razi uses medical evidence of crisis to prove that the soul is independent of the body and does not die when the body dies.

Core Idea
The soul's immunity to illness proves its independence from the body.

Ar-Razi presents a sophisticated medical argument to demonstrate the soul's independence. He observes that during a medical crisis, the soul remains strong while the body weakens. This leads to the conclusion that the soul does not die with the body and is distinct from it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation. Let the argument's flow come through.
Notice the logical connectors like 'فوجب', 'إما أن', 'فالأول باطل'.
2
Understand the premise
The argument begins with the claim that the soul does not become ill with the body. This is the key observation.
The entire proof rests on this premise.
3
Follow the reasoning about 'nature' and crisis
Ar-Razi uses the medical concept of 'buhran' (crisis) to identify a 'nature' that resists disease. Follow his reasoning to see why this nature cannot be the body or its qualities.
The two reasons given are crucial: (1) contradiction of attributes, (2) simultaneous extreme weakness and strength.
4
Analyze the soul's role in crisis
Once the nature is identified as the soul, consider why the soul must be strong and not ill during crisis. This shows its independence from bodily illness.
The argument uses the principle that the overcome cannot resist the overcomer.
5
Conclude the proof
Since the soul is independent and unaffected by bodily illness, death of the body cannot necessitate death of the soul. The argument also demonstrates the soul is distinct from the body.
Ar-Razi calls this a 'strong and appropriate statement'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الخامسة في بيان أن النفس لا تموت بموت البدن : نقول : إن النفس لا تمرض بمرض البدن ، فوجب أن لا تموت بموت البدن . إنما قلنا : إنها لا تمرض بمرض البدن ، وذلك لأن الشواهد الطبية دالة على أنه لا معنى للبحران إلا حصول المقاومة بين الطبيعة وبين العلة ، فهذه الطبيعة التي تقاوم العلة ، إما أن تكون هي مزاج البدن ، أو كيفية [ من الكيفيات ] القائمة بالبدن ، وإما أن تكون هي النفس . والأول باطل لوجهين : أحدهما : إن جسم البدن موصوف بالكيفيات المرضية المنافية للصحة فلو كان هو بعينه موصوفا بالكيفيات الصحية الملائمة للصحة ، لزم كون الجسم الواحد [ في الوقت الواحد ] موصوفاً بصفتين متضادتين . وهو محال . وثانيهما : إن البدن حصل في حقه أسباب ثلاثة ، كل واحد منها يوجب الضعف . فأحدها : الحرارة الغريزية العرضية ، الموجبة لتحلل الرطوبات الكثيرة . وثانيها : إن الحرارة الغريزية أيضاً موجبة لتحلل الرطوبات على قياس ما كان حال الصحة . وثالثها : إن في وقت البحران تنقطع الطبيعة عن الاغتذاء ، وقد يبقى المريض منقطعاً عن الاغتذاء أياماً كثيرة ، وهو سبب لحصول الضعف . فثبت : أن البدن في غاية الضعف ، والطبيعة في غاية القوة على الدفع ، فلو كانت هذه الطبيعة هي البدن ، أو جزء من أجزاء البدن ، لزم كون الشيء الواحد موصوفاً بغاية الضعف ، وبغاية القوة . وهو محال . فثبت : أن الشيء الذي يقاوم العلة هو النفس . فنقول : النفس في تلك الحالة ، إما أن تكون مريضة ضعيفة وإما أن تكون خالية من المرض والضعف . والأول باطل . لأن النفس في هذه الحالة ، لو كانت مريضة ضعيفة ، لما قدرت على مقاومة العلة الغالبة ، والمادة القاهرة المبطلة . لأن المغلوب لا يمكنه مقاومة الغالب [ والمقهور لا يمكنه مقاومة القاهر ] فثبت بهذا البيان الظاهر : أن النفس في تلك الحالة قوية قاهرة ، سليمة عن الضعف والمرض - وظاهر أن البدن في غاية الضعف والمرض وذلك يدل على أن النفس لا تمرض بمرض البدن ولا تضعف بضعفه البتة . وإذا ثبت هذا ، وجب أن لا تموت بموته . وذلك لأن النفس لما لم تمرض بمرض البدن ، ولم تضعف بضعفه ، ظهر أن النفس غنية في ذاتها وفي كمال قدرتها وقوتها عن هذا البدن . فإذا مات البدن ، فقد مات شيء كانت النفس غنية في ذاتها وفي قدرتها وفي علمها عنه . ومتى كان الأمر كذلك ، امتنع أن يكون موت البدن ، موجباً لموت النفس . وهذا كلام قوي مناسب . وهو بعينه يدل على أن النفس غير البدن ، وغير جميع أجزائه وأبعاضه .
The fifth proof in showing that the soul does not die with the death of the body: We say: The soul does not become ill with the illness of the body, so it must not die with the death of the body. We say: It does not become ill with the illness of the body, because medical evidences indicate that there is no meaning to crisis except the occurrence of resistance between the nature and the disease. So this nature that resists the disease is either the temperament of the body, or a quality from among the qualities subsisting in the body, or it is the soul. The first is invalid for two reasons: One of them: The body is described with pathological qualities contrary to health; if it were itself described with healthful qualities compatible with health, it would necessitate one body [at one time] being described with two contradictory attributes, which is impossible. The second: The body has three causes that each necessitate weakness: the first is the accidental innate heat causing dissolution of many humors; the second is that the innate heat also causes dissolution of humors similar to what was the case in health; the third is that at the time of crisis the nature stops nourishment, and the patient may remain without nourishment for many days, which is a cause of weakness. So it is established that the body is at the extreme of weakness, and the nature is at the extreme of strength in repelling. If this nature were the body or a part of the body, it would necessitate one thing being described with extreme weakness and extreme strength, which is impossible. So it is established that the thing that resists the disease is the soul. Then we say: The soul in that state is either ill and weak or free from illness and weakness. The first is invalid because the soul in that state, if it were ill and weak, would not be able to resist the overpowering disease and the overwhelming nullifying matter; for the overcome cannot resist the overcomer, and the overpowered cannot resist the over powerer. So it is established by this clear demonstration that the soul in that state is strong and overpowering, free from weakness and illness. And it is apparent that the body is at the extreme of weakness and illness. That indicates that the soul does not become ill with the illness of the body nor does it weaken with its weakening at all. And when this is established, it must not die with its death. That is because the soul, since it did not become ill with the illness of the body and did not weaken with its weakening, it appears that the soul is independent in its essence and in the perfection of its power and strength from this body. So when the body dies, something has died that the soul was independent of in its essence, its power, and its knowledge. And when the matter is thus, it is impossible that the death of the body necessitates the death of the soul. And this is a strong and appropriate statement. And it itself indicates that the soul is other than the body and other than all its parts and limbs.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth proof that the soul does not die with the death of the body. The proof is structured as a causal argument based on the observed fact that the soul does not become ill when the body is ill. The author begins by asserting this premise and then justifies it through medical analysis of the phenomenon of 'buhran' (crisis). He explains that during a medical crisis, there is a resistance between a 'nature' and the disease. This resisting nature must be identified. It cannot be the body's temperament or a quality in the body, because that would lead to contradictions: the body would have to be simultaneously healthy and ill, or extremely weak and extremely strong. Therefore, the resisting element must be the soul. Then he argues that the soul during crisis cannot be ill or weak, because if it were, it could not resist the overpowering disease. Hence the soul is strong and healthy. Since the body is weak and ill, the soul is independent of the body. Consequently, the soul's death does not follow from the body's death. The argument also demonstrates that the soul is distinct from the body and its parts. The author concludes that this is a strong and appropriate argument.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The soul's health depends on bodily health; if the body is ill, the soul also becomes ill.
Correction: The argument shows that during bodily illness, the soul remains strong and resists the disease, proving its independence from the body's condition.

Checkpoint
According to the fifth argument, why must the soul not die with the body?
A) Because the soul is made of a different substance
B) Because the soul does not become ill when the body is ill
C) Because the soul is eternal
D) Because the soul resides in the heart

Key Takeaway
The soul's independence from bodily illness proves that it does not die with the body and is distinct from it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When your body is weak, ill, or in pain, do you consciously turn to your soul (your inner self) as a source of strength and resistance? How can you cultivate that awareness starting today?
?
Ar-Razi proves that the soul remains strong and unaffected even as the body dies. If you truly believed this, how would it change your fear of death and your attachment to worldly health? What practical step can you take to strengthen your soul now?
?
If your soul is independent and does not die with your body, what does that mean for how you invest your time and energy? Are you feeding your soul or only your body? Commit to one daily action that nourishes your soul.

Causal Argument for the Soul's Immortality
First part of the sixth proof: causal argument and accidental nature of soul-body relation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof that the soul survives the body because its essence depends on permanent higher causes, not on its accidental relation to the body.

Core Idea
The soul's permanence is necessitated by its permanent higher causes, not by its temporary body relation.

This lesson presents the first part of the sixth rational proof for the soul's immortality. The author establishes that the soul is a pure substance effected by a higher intellectual substance, while its attachment to the body is merely accidental. At death, the accidental relation ceases, but the higher causes remain, thus the soul must persist.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get a sense of the argument's flow. Note how the author starts by recalling prior proofs.
2
Identify the two key distinctions
Notice the contrast between the soul's essence (pure substance, effect of higher cause) and its attachment to the body (accidental relation). Also distinguish between permanent higher causes and temporary additions.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Consider why the author says it would be absurd to prefer the weak accidental matter over the strong essential matter. Understand that this forces the conclusion that the soul is immortal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السادسة في بيان أن النفس لا تموت بموت البدن : إنا قد دللنا على أن جوهر النفس من جنس جوهر الملائكة ، ودللنا على أن المؤثر في وجوده ، لا بد وأن يكون جوهراً عقلياً مجرداً ودللنا على أن المقتضى لحدوث العلوم والمعارف في ذاته جوهر عقلي مجرد فالنفس في ذاتها جوهر مجرد وهو معلول جوهر مجرد وصفاته معلولات الجوهر المجرد . وأما تعلقها بهذا البدن ، فليس إلا على سبيل التدبير والتصرف، وهذا التدبير والتصرف من باب النسب والإضافات ، وهي أضعف أنواع الموجودات. ومع ذلك فهي من العوارض العارضة لذات النفس . إذا عرفت هذا فنقول : الحاصل عند موت البدن زوال هذه الإضافة وأما العلل العالية المؤثرة في ذات النفس وفي جميع صفاتها الحقيقية باقية. وبقاؤها يقتضي بقاء جوهر النفس ، وبقاء جميع صفاتها العالية. فلو قلنا : بأنها تعدم عند زوال هذه الإضافة لكنا قد رجحنا مقتضى الأمر العرضي ، البالغ في الضعف إلى أقصى الغايات على مقتضى الأمر الذاتي الأصلي، البالغ في الكمال والقوة إلى أقصى الغايات . ومعلوم أن ذلك باطل في بديهة العقل، فوجب القطع بأن النفس لا تموت بموت البدن . ثم ههنا دقيقة أخرى. وهي : إنا قد ذكرنا في أول هذا الكتاب الذي سميناه بكتاب الأرواح العالية والسافلة ، أن الموجودات لها ثلاثة مراتب ، فأشرفها عالم الإله ، وأخسها عالم الجسم - وهو عالم الهيولى - وأوسطها عالم الأرواح . فإنها تقبل إشراق عالم الإله. وبواسطة ذلك الإشراق تقوى على التأثير في عالم الهيولي . إذا عرفت هذا فنقول : تعلق النفس بالبدن على سبيل التدبير والتصرف . عبارة عن تعلق النفس بالجانب الأخس الأدون العاري عن التأثير والفعل . وكون النفس مستنيرة بأنوار معارف عالم الإله ، عبارة عن تعلقها بالجانب الأفضل الأكمل ، الذي هو ينبوع القوة والبقاء والدوام . فلو قلنا : إن عند زوال العلاقة الخسيسة - أعني تدبير البدن - تبطل ذاتها ومعرفتها . لكنا قد حكمنا بأن الجانب الأخس الأضعف ، هو الجانب الأشرف الأقوى . وذلك محال
The sixth proof that the soul does not die with the death of the body: We have demonstrated that the substance (jawhar) of the soul is of the same kind as the substance of the angels, and we have demonstrated that the effecter in its existence must be a purely intellectual substance (jawhar 'aqli mujarrad), and we have demonstrated that that which necessitates the occurrence of sciences and cognitions in its essence is a purely intellectual substance. So the soul in its essence is a pure substance (jawhar mujarrad) and it is an effect of a pure substance, and its attributes are effects of the pure substance. As for its attachment (ta'alluq) to this body, it is only by way of management (tadbir) and disposition (tasarruf), and this management and disposition belong to the category of relations (nisab) and additions (idafat), which are the weakest of existents. Nevertheless, they are accidents (awarid) that attach to the essence of the soul. If you know this, we say: What obtains (al-hasil) at the death of the body is the cessation of this addition. As for the higher causes (al-'ilal al-'aliyah) that effect the essence of the soul and all its real attributes, they remain. Their permanence necessitates the permanence of the substance of the soul and the permanence of all its higher attributes. So if we say that it becomes non-existent at the cessation of this addition, we would have given precedence to the implication of the accidental matter (al-amr al-'aradi), which has reached the utmost limit of weakness, over the implication of the essential, original matter (al-amr al-dhati al-asli), which has reached the utmost limit of perfection and strength. It is well known that this is false in the first principles of the intellect (badihah al-'aql), so it is necessary to be certain that the soul does not die with the death of the body. Then here is another subtle point (dabiqah ukhra). It is: We have mentioned at the beginning of this book, which we have named 'The High and Low Spirits' (al-Arwah al-'Aliyah wa al-Safilah), that existents have three levels: the most noble is the world of the Divine ('alam al-ilah), the lowest is the world of body ('alam al-jism) which is the world of hyle ('alam al-hayula), and the middle is the world of spirits ('alam al-arwah). For they receive the radiance (ishraq) of the world of the Divine, and through that radiance they become strong enough to effect [change] in the world of hyle. If you know this, we say: The attachment of the soul to the body by way of management and disposition is an expression of the soul's attachment to the lower, baser side that is devoid of effect and action. And the soul's being illuminated by the lights of the cognitions of the world of the Divine is an expression of its attachment to the superior, more perfect side, which is the source of strength, permanence, and constancy. So if we said that upon the cessation of the base relationship—i.e., management of the body—its essence and its cognition become invalid (tabtul), we would have judged that the lower, weaker side is the nobler, stronger side. That is impossible (muhal).
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage is the sixth rational proof (al-hujjah al-sadisah) demonstrating that the soul does not die with the body. It consists of two parts: a causal argument and a subtle point about the hierarchy of existence. The author begins by recalling earlier proofs that the substance (jawhar) of the soul is like the substance of angels, that its cause (mu'aththir) must be a purely intellectual substance (jawhar 'aqli mujarrad), and that the source of its knowledge is also a purely intellectual substance. Thus the soul itself is a pure substance, an effect of a pure substance, and its attributes are effects of that same substance. In contrast, its attachment to the body is merely by way of management and disposition (tadbir wa tasarruf), which is a relation (nisbah) and addition (idafah)—the weakest category of existents. These are accidents ('awarid) attaching to the soul's essence. At death, this relational addition disappears, but the higher causes that gave existence to the soul and its real attributes remain. Since these causes persist, they necessitate the continued existence of the soul's substance and its attributes. To claim that the soul ceases with the cessation of the accidental relation would be to prefer the implication of the weak accidental matter over the implication of the essential, original matter, which is absurd according to the first principles of reason. Hence the soul must be immortal. The second part presents a subtle point (dabiqah) from the author's earlier work 'The High and Low Spirits.' He explains that existents have three ranks: the highest is the world of the Divine, the lowest is the corporeal world (world of hyle), and the intermediate is the world of spirits. The spirits receive radiance from the Divine world and thereby gain the strength to affect the lower world. The soul's attachment to the body is its connection to the lower, baser side, while its illumination by divine knowledge is its connection to the higher, perfect side. If one claimed that the loss of the base relationship (body management) annihilates the soul's essence and knowledge, one would be treating the weaker side as nobler than the stronger side, which is impossible. Thus the soul's immortality is further confirmed.

Key Terms
الجوهر المجرد (al-jawhar al-mujarrad)
العلة العالية (al-illah al-'aliyah)
التعلق (al-ta'alluq)
التدبير والتصرف (al-tadbir wa al-tasarruf)
الإضافة (al-idafah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The soul's existence depends on the body because its management ceases at death.
Correction: The soul's management of the body is an accidental relation, not essential. Its essence depends on permanent higher causes, which remain after death.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens to the soul's higher causes at death?
A) They cease along with the body.
B) They become weaker.
C) They remain permanent.
D) They are replaced by new causes.

Key Takeaway
The soul's existence is necessitated by its permanent higher causes, not by its accidental relation to the body, so it must survive the body's death.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your soul's existence does not depend on your body, what does that mean for how you value your physical life versus your spiritual life? Are you currently living as if your body is essential to your identity?
?
The argument says that giving priority to the accidental over the essential is intellectually false. Where in your daily choices do you prioritize temporary, accidental matters over your soul's permanent reality?
?
Knowing that your soul will survive death, how should that change your attitude toward fear of death or attachment to worldly things? What concrete step can you take today to live more in light of this truth?

Hierarchy of Existence and the Soul's Immortality
Second part of the sixth proof: subtle argument from the hierarchy of existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the subtle point that the soul's attachment to the lower bodily realm is weaker than its essential connection to the higher divine realm, so the loss of the body cannot annihilate the soul.

Core Idea
The soul's connection to the divine is essential and permanent; its bodily connection is accidental and inferior.

This lesson presents a subtle additional proof based on a three-tier hierarchy of existence: the divine world, the world of spirits, and the corporeal world. The soul has two attachments: one to the lower body (management) and one to the higher divine realm (illumination). Since the higher attachment is stronger and more essential, the loss of the lower attachment cannot destroy the soul.

Guided Path
1
Understand the three-level hierarchy
The author describes three worlds: the divine, the spirits, and the corporeal (hyle). Note the properties of each and their relationships.
The spirits receive radiance from the divine and then affect the corporeal.
2
Identify the soul's two attachments
The soul attaches to the body via management (lower, weak) and to the divine via illumination (higher, strong). Recognize which is essential.
3
Reason from the hierarchy
If the soul ceased with the loss of the lower attachment, that would mean the weaker determines the stronger—an impossibility. Conclude the soul persists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السادسة في بيان أن النفس لا تموت بموت البدن : إنا قد دللنا على أن جوهر النفس من جنس جوهر الملائكة ، ودللنا على أن المؤثر في وجوده ، لا بد وأن يكون جوهراً عقلياً مجرداً ودللنا على أن المقتضى لحدوث العلوم والمعارف في ذاته جوهر عقلي مجرد فالنفس في ذاتها جوهر مجرد وهو معلول جوهر مجرد وصفاته معلولات الجوهر المجرد . وأما تعلقها بهذا البدن ، فليس إلا على سبيل التدبير والتصرف، وهذا التدبير والتصرف من باب النسب والإضافات ، وهي أضعف أنواع الموجودات. ومع ذلك فهي من العوارض العارضة لذات النفس . إذا عرفت هذا فنقول : الحاصل عند موت البدن زوال هذه الإضافة وأما العلل العالية المؤثرة في ذات النفس وفي جميع صفاتها الحقيقية باقية. وبقاؤها يقتضي بقاء جوهر النفس ، وبقاء جميع صفاتها العالية. فلو قلنا : بأنها تعدم عند زوال هذه الإضافة لكنا قد رجحنا مقتضى الأمر العرضي ، البالغ في الضعف إلى أقصى الغايات على مقتضى الأمر الذاتي الأصلي، البالغ في الكمال والقوة إلى أقصى الغايات . ومعلوم أن ذلك باطل في بديهة العقل، فوجب القطع بأن النفس لا تموت بموت البدن . ثم ههنا دقيقة أخرى. وهي : إنا قد ذكرنا في أول هذا الكتاب الذي سميناه بكتاب الأرواح العالية والسافلة ، أن الموجودات لها ثلاثة مراتب ، فأشرفها عالم الإله ، وأخسها عالم الجسم - وهو عالم الهيولى - وأوسطها عالم الأرواح . فإنها تقبل إشراق عالم الإله. وبواسطة ذلك الإشراق تقوى على التأثير في عالم الهيولي . إذا عرفت هذا فنقول : تعلق النفس بالبدن على سبيل التدبير والتصرف . عبارة عن تعلق النفس بالجانب الأخس الأدون العاري عن التأثير والفعل . وكون النفس مستنيرة بأنوار معارف عالم الإله ، عبارة عن تعلقها بالجانب الأفضل الأكمل ، الذي هو ينبوع القوة والبقاء والدوام . فلو قلنا : إن عند زوال العلاقة الخسيسة - أعني تدبير البدن - تبطل ذاتها ومعرفتها . لكنا قد حكمنا بأن الجانب الأخس الأضعف ، هو الجانب الأشرف الأقوى . وذلك محال
The sixth proof that the soul does not die with the death of the body: We have demonstrated that the substance (jawhar) of the soul is of the same kind as the substance of the angels, and we have demonstrated that the effecter in its existence must be a purely intellectual substance (jawhar 'aqli mujarrad), and we have demonstrated that that which necessitates the occurrence of sciences and cognitions in its essence is a purely intellectual substance. So the soul in its essence is a pure substance (jawhar mujarrad) and it is an effect of a pure substance, and its attributes are effects of the pure substance. As for its attachment (ta'alluq) to this body, it is only by way of management (tadbir) and disposition (tasarruf), and this management and disposition belong to the category of relations (nisab) and additions (idafat), which are the weakest of existents. Nevertheless, they are accidents (awarid) that attach to the essence of the soul. If you know this, we say: What obtains (al-hasil) at the death of the body is the cessation of this addition. As for the higher causes (al-'ilal al-'aliyah) that effect the essence of the soul and all its real attributes, they remain. Their permanence necessitates the permanence of the substance of the soul and the permanence of all its higher attributes. So if we say that it becomes non-existent at the cessation of this addition, we would have given precedence to the implication of the accidental matter (al-amr al-'aradi), which has reached the utmost limit of weakness, over the implication of the essential, original matter (al-amr al-dhati al-asli), which has reached the utmost limit of perfection and strength. It is well known that this is false in the first principles of the intellect (badihah al-'aql), so it is necessary to be certain that the soul does not die with the death of the body. Then here is another subtle point (dabiqah ukhra). It is: We have mentioned at the beginning of this book, which we have named 'The High and Low Spirits' (al-Arwah al-'Aliyah wa al-Safilah), that existents have three levels: the most noble is the world of the Divine ('alam al-ilah), the lowest is the world of body ('alam al-jism) which is the world of hyle ('alam al-hayula), and the middle is the world of spirits ('alam al-arwah). For they receive the radiance (ishraq) of the world of the Divine, and through that radiance they become strong enough to effect [change] in the world of hyle. If you know this, we say: The attachment of the soul to the body by way of management and disposition is an expression of the soul's attachment to the lower, baser side that is devoid of effect and action. And the soul's being illuminated by the lights of the cognitions of the world of the Divine is an expression of its attachment to the superior, more perfect side, which is the source of strength, permanence, and constancy. So if we said that upon the cessation of the base relationship—i.e., management of the body—its essence and its cognition become invalid (tabtul), we would have judged that the lower, weaker side is the nobler, stronger side. That is impossible (muhal).
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage is the sixth rational proof (al-hujjah al-sadisah) demonstrating that the soul does not die with the body. It consists of two parts: a causal argument and a subtle point about the hierarchy of existence. The author begins by recalling earlier proofs that the substance (jawhar) of the soul is like the substance of angels, that its cause (mu'aththir) must be a purely intellectual substance (jawhar 'aqli mujarrad), and that the source of its knowledge is also a purely intellectual substance. Thus the soul itself is a pure substance, an effect of a pure substance, and its attributes are effects of that same substance. In contrast, its attachment to the body is merely by way of management and disposition (tadbir wa tasarruf), which is a relation (nisbah) and addition (idafah)—the weakest category of existents. These are accidents ('awarid) attaching to the soul's essence. At death, this relational addition disappears, but the higher causes that gave existence to the soul and its real attributes remain. Since these causes persist, they necessitate the continued existence of the soul's substance and its attributes. To claim that the soul ceases with the cessation of the accidental relation would be to prefer the implication of the weak accidental matter over the implication of the essential, original matter, which is absurd according to the first principles of reason. Hence the soul must be immortal. The second part presents a subtle point (dabiqah) from the author's earlier work 'The High and Low Spirits.' He explains that existents have three ranks: the highest is the world of the Divine, the lowest is the corporeal world (world of hyle), and the intermediate is the world of spirits. The spirits receive radiance from the Divine world and thereby gain the strength to affect the lower world. The soul's attachment to the body is its connection to the lower, baser side, while its illumination by divine knowledge is its connection to the higher, perfect side. If one claimed that the loss of the base relationship (body management) annihilates the soul's essence and knowledge, one would be treating the weaker side as nobler than the stronger side, which is impossible. Thus the soul's immortality is further confirmed.

Key Terms
عالم الأرواح ('alam al-arwah)
عالم الهيولى ('alam al-hayula)
عالم الإله ('alam al-ilah)
الإشراق (ishraq)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The soul's management of the body is essential to its existence, so when management stops, the soul ceases.
Correction: The management is a lower, accidental attachment; the soul's essential attachment is to the Divine, which is permanent.

Checkpoint
What does the author identify as the 'source of strength, permanence, and constancy' for the soul?
A) The world of hyle.
B) The world of spirits.
C) The world of the Divine.
D) The soul's management of the body.

Key Takeaway
The soul's essential connection to the divine realm ensures its immortality, regardless of the loss of its accidental bodily management.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your body were to fail completely, do you have an inner connection to God that would sustain you? This lesson says your soul is illuminated by divine knowledge. Have you cultivated that illumination, or have you relied solely on physical acts of worship that may cease? What step will you take today to strengthen that inner light?
?
The passage describes the body as 'lower, baser side devoid of effect and action.' Yet you spend most of your time managing your body. Does that priority align with the lesson's teaching that your essential self is attached to the Divine? What would change if you truly believed that your most real connection is to God, not to your body?
?
The author argues that it is impossible for the weaker side to be more essential than the stronger side. Examine your own life: which side do you treat as essential? Do your daily choices reflect a belief that your soul's genuine strength comes from God, or from your physical abilities? Commit to one concrete action today that shifts your focus from body management to divine illumination.

The Persistence of the Soul's Essential Attributes
Main argument that the soul persists because its essential attributes remain after bodily death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the soul's essential attributes persist even after the body dies, based on the distinction between essential causes and accidental relations.

Core Idea
The soul's true essence is independent of the body; only its accidental relation perishes.

In this passage, the author presents a rational argument for the soul's survival after death. He distinguishes between the soul's essential attributes, which remain, and its accidental relation to the body, which dissolves. This foundation is crucial for understanding life after death in Islamic thought.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the key distinction
Look for how the author separates the soul's essence from its relation to the body. Note that the relation is an accident (عرض).
The Arabic terms are crucial here.
2
Understand the causal logic
The author argues that the higher causes (العلل العالية) remain, so the soul's essence remains. Why would the loss of a relation not affect the essence?
3
Reflect on the reductio ad absurdum
If the soul perished with the body, we would be valuing a weak accidental relation over a strong essential one. Why is this absurd?
This is a key rational intuition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جوهر مجرد وصفاته معلولات الجوهر المجرد. وأما تعلقها بهذا البدن، فليس إلا على سبيل التدبير والتصرف، وهذا التدبير والتصرف من باب النسب والإضافات، وهي أضعف أنواع الموجودات. ومع ذلك فهي من العوارض العارضة لذات النفس. إذا عرفت هذا فنقول: الحاصل عند موت البدن زوال هذه الإضافة. وأما العلل العالية المؤثرة في ذات النفس وفي جميع صفاتها الحقيقية باقية. وبقاؤها يقتضي بقاء جوهر النفس، وبقاء جميع صفاتها العالية. فلو قلنا بأنها تعدم عند زوال هذه الإضافة لكنا قد رجحنا مقتضى الأمر العرضي، البالغ في الضعف إلى أقصى الغايات على مقتضى الأمر الذاتي الأصلي، البالغ في الكمال والقوة إلى أقصى الغايات. ومعلوم أن ذلك باطل في بديهة العقل، فوجب القطع بأن النفس لا تموت بموت البدن. ثم ههنا دقيقة أخرى. وهي: إنا قد ذكرنا في أول هذا الكتاب الذي سميناه بكتاب (الأرواح العالية والسافلة)، أن الموجودات لها ثلاثة مراتب، فأشرفها عالم الإله، وأختها عالم الجسم - وهو عالم الهيولى - وأوسطها عالم الأرواح. فإنها تقبل إشراق عالم الإله. وبواسطة ذلك الإشراق تقوى على التأثير في عالم الهيولي. إذا عرفت هذا فنقول: تعلق النفس بالبدن على سبيل التدبير والتصرف عبارة عن تعلق النفس بالجانب الأخس الأدون العاري عن التأثير والفعل. وكون النفس مستنيرة بأنوار معارف عالم الإله، عبارة عن تعلقها بالجانب الأفضل الأكمل، الذي هو ينبوع القوة والبقاء والدوام. فلو قلنا إن عند زوال العلاقة الخسيسة - أعني تدبير البدن - تبطل ذاتها ومعرفتها. لكنا قد حكمنا بأن الجانب الأخس الأضعف، هو الجانب الأشرف الأقوى. وذلك محال. فوجب أن لا تموت النفس بموت البدن.
A simple substance, and its attributes are effects of the simple substance. As for its attachment to this body, it is only by way of management and action, and this management and action are of the category of relations and additions, and they are the weakest types of existents. Yet they are among the accidents that accrue to the essence of the soul. If you know this, we say: What results at the death of the body is the removal of this addition. As for the higher causes that affect the essence of the soul and all its real attributes, they are remaining. Their persistence necessitates the persistence of the essence of the soul and the persistence of all its high attributes. So if we said that it is annihilated when this addition is removed, we would have preferred the implication of the accidental matter, which reaches the utmost weakness, over the implication of the original essential matter, which reaches the utmost perfection and strength. And it is known that this is false in the primary intuition of reason, so it is necessary to be certain that the soul does not die with the death of the body. Then there is another subtle point. That is: We have mentioned at the beginning of this book, which we named 'The High and Low Spirits', that existents have three ranks: the most noble is the divine world, and the lowest is the corporeal world—which is the world of matter—and the middle is the world of spirits. For they receive illumination from the divine world, and by means of that illumination they become strong to have effect in the world of matter. If you know this, we say: The attachment of the soul to the body by way of management and action is an expression of the soul's attachment to the lower, inferior side, devoid of effect and action. And the soul's being illuminated by the lights of the knowledge of the divine world is an expression of its attachment to the better, more perfect side, which is the source of strength, permanence, and eternity. So if we said that upon the removal of the base relationship—I mean the management of the body—its essence and knowledge become null, we would have judged that the lower, weaker side is the nobler, stronger side. And that is impossible. So it is necessary that the soul does not die with the death of the body.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is a proof that the soul does not die with the body. The author begins by establishing that the soul is a simple substance (جوهر مجرد) and that its attributes are effects of that substance. Its connection to the body is only through management and action, which are relations (نسب وإضافات)—the weakest type of existence. These relations are accidents (عوارض) that accrue to the soul's essence. Once this is understood, the author states that what is lost at the death of the body is just this relation (إضافة), but the higher causes (العلل العالية) that affect the soul's essence and all its real attributes remain. Their persistence necessitates the persistence of the soul's essence and all its high attributes. If we claimed that the soul is annihilated when this relation is lost, we would be giving priority to a contingent accidental matter, which is extremely weak, over the original essential matter, which is extremely strong and perfect. This is clearly false to reason, so we must conclude that the soul does not die with the body. Then the author adds a further subtle point (دقيقة أخرى): He previously mentioned in his book 'The High and Low Spirits' that existents have three ranks: the highest is the divine world, the lowest is the corporeal world (of matter), and the intermediate is the world of spirits. The spirits receive illumination from the divine world, and through that illumination they become able to influence the material world. So the soul's attachment to the body for management is its attachment to the lower, deficient side lacking action, while the soul's illumination with the lights of divine knowledge is its attachment to the better, perfect side, the source of power, permanence, and eternity. If we said that the soul and its knowledge vanish when the low connection (body management) is lost, we would be judging that the lower, weaker side is the nobler, stronger side, which is impossible. Therefore, the soul must not die with the death of the body.

Key Terms
النفس
الجوهر المجرد
العوارض
الإضافة
العلل العالية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the soul is an accident that perishes with the body.
Correction: The author argues it is a substance whose essential attributes remain; only the accidental relation to the body is lost.

Checkpoint
According to the first argument, what happens to the soul's essential attributes when the body dies?
A) They perish along with the body.
B) They remain because the higher causes affecting them persist.
C) They become part of the body.
D) They are transformed into accidents.

Key Takeaway
The soul's essence remains after death because its essential attributes are independent of the body's demise.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the deepest attachments of your life—to people, roles, achievements—are only accidents (إضافات) that can be removed at death, what is left of you that is truly your own? Are you building your life around what perishes or what remains?
?
The author argues that preferring the accidental over the essential is 'false in the primary intuition of reason.' Yet how often do you live as if worldly comforts are more real than your soul's survival? What would change if you truly saw them as the weakest of existents?
?
You will face death alone, stripped of every relation to this body. What 'higher causes'—what lasting connection to Allah—have you secured that will keep your essence intact? If you were to die tonight, would you be certain that your soul's attributes are real and enduring?

The Three Ranks and the Soul's Connection to the Divine
Further subtle point using the three ranks of existence to reinforce the soul's persistence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three ranks of existence and how the soul's connection to the divine world ensures its permanence beyond bodily death.

Core Idea
The soul's nobility lies in its connection to the divine, not the body.

The author then deepens the argument by introducing a cosmological framework. He explains that the soul belongs to a middle realm between the divine and material worlds, receiving illumination from above. This higher connection ensures the soul's permanence when its bodily tie is severed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three ranks of existence
The author lists three worlds: divine, spiritual, and material. Which one is the soul?
2
Analyze the soul's two attachments
The soul is attached to the body (low) and to divine knowledge (high). Which is stronger?
The author uses this to argue from the stronger.
3
Understand the conclusion
Since the soul's higher attachment is nobler and more permanent, losing the lower attachment does not cause annihilation.
This reinforces the first argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The Soul's Independence in Thought and Action
Seventh proof: soul's theoretical and practical powers independent of body

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the seventh proof for the soul's immortality, which argues that both the theoretical and practical powers of the soul are independent of the body.

Core Idea
The soul does not depend on the body; it acquires knowledge directly from a higher realm.

In this passage, the author presents a detailed proof that the soul continues to exist after the body's death. He shows that the soul's two fundamental operations—thinking and acting—do not require the body at all. The argument traces the logical steps from concept formation to practical governance, demonstrating independence at every stage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two powers of the soul
Read the opening lines where the author states that the soul has two powers: theoretical and practical. Note the definitions given.
The theoretical power deals with acquiring knowledge; the practical power deals with managing the body.
2
Follow the proof for theoretical power
Trace the argument: concepts reside in the soul, they emanate from higher causes, then judgments and syllogisms arise—all without needing the body.
Look for the sequence: preparedness, emanation, concept, judgment, self-evident propositions, middle term, conclusion.
3
Understand the independence of practical power
The body is the locus of this power's action, not its cause. The body is receptive to the soul, so it cannot be an agent over the soul.
The author gives two reasons: the body is a locus, not a cause; and the receptive cannot be the agent.
4
Reflect on the final claim about essence
The author notes that the soul is independent in its essence, promising further evidence that its cause cannot be a body.
This part is previewed but not fully argued here.
