Second Proof: The Soul Cannot Be Annihilated
Second proof for the soul's incorruptibility via division and refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical structure of the second proof for the soul's incorruptibility, including its division into two possible causes of annihilation and the refutation of the first cause.

Core Idea
The soul's annihilation is impossible because any cause leads to absurdity.

This passage presents a refined argument for the soul's permanence. The author divides possible causes of annihilation into two exhaustive categories: either the existence of something the soul needs absent, or the absence of something the soul needs present. Then he refutes the first category, showing it leads to a logical impasse. This lesson traces the argument up to the introduction of the first reason for its impossibility.

Guided Path
1
Understand the division
Read the first sentence: 'If it were annihilated... either due to the existence of something whose non-existence the soul needed, or due to the non-existence of something whose existence the soul needed.' Notice that these two possibilities cover all logical options.
The author calls the division 'apparent' (ظاهر).
2
Examine the refutation of the first division
Focus on the claim that the thing causing annihilation must be an opposite (ضد) of the soul's substance, and that this opposite must arise after the soul's existence. Understand why the author says this is necessary.
3
Analyze the first reason
The author gives the first reason why this is impossible: opposition is mutual. So it is not more likely that the soul is destroyed by the opposite's occurrence than that the opposite is repelled by the soul's persistence. Ask yourself what additional reason might be needed to decide priority.
The passage cuts off here, but the reasoning is clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية في بيان أن النفس الناطقة لا تقبل الفساد : إنها لو عدمت بعد وجودها ، لكان عدمها لا بد وأن يكون ، إما لوجود شيء ، كانت النفس محتاجة إلى عدمه ، أو لعدم شيء كانت النفس محتاجة إلى وجوده . والقسمان باطلان ، فبطل القول بعدمها. أما الحصر فظاهر ، وأما بيان فساد القسم الأول وهو أن النفس تعدم لوجود شيء كانت النفس محتاجة إلى عدمه . فهو أن نقول : إن ذلك الشيء يجب أن يكون ضـداً لجـوهـر النفس ، ويجب أن يقال : إن ذلك الضد ما كان موجوداً حال بقاء النفس ، وإنما حدث بعد ذلك . وهو محال لوجوه : الأول : إن المضادة حاصلة من الجانبين ، فلم يكن فناء النفس لأجل حدوث ذلك الضد ، أولى من اندفاع ذلك الضد ، لأجل قيام النفس ، بل هذا
The second proof in demonstrating that the rational soul does not accept corruption: If it were annihilated after its existence, its annihilation would have to be either due to the existence of something whose non-existence the soul needed, or due to the non-existence of something whose existence the soul needed. And both divisions are invalid, so the claim of its annihilation is invalid. As for the division, it is apparent. As for demonstrating the corruption of the first division—that the soul is annihilated due to the existence of something whose non-existence the soul needed—it is that we say: That thing must be an opposite (didd) to the substance of the soul, and it must be said that that opposite was not existent at the time of the soul's remaining, but rather occurred after that. And that is impossible for [several] reasons: The first: Oppositeness (mudaada) is from both sides, so the annihilation of the soul due to the occurrence of that opposite is not more likely than the repulsion of that opposite due to the soul's persistence; rather, this...
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage introduces the second proof for the soul's incorruptibility. The proof proceeds by division: if the soul is annihilated after existence, the cause must be either the existence of something whose non-existence the soul needs, or the non-existence of something whose existence the soul needs. Both are impossible. The author then refutes the first division: the thing whose existence causes the soul's annihilation must be an opposite (ضد) of the soul's substance, and it must arise after the soul's existence. This is impossible because the opposition is mutual; it is not more plausible that the soul is destroyed by the opposite's occurrence than that the opposite is repelled by the soul's persistence. The argument is cut off at 'بل هذا' but the reasoning is clear: the opposite cannot overcome the soul without a reason for priority.

Key Terms
عدم
ضد
مضادة
نفس ناطقة
فساد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The soul can cease to exist due to an external cause like the body's decay.
Correction: The proof shows that any external cause must be an opposite with mutual opposition, which cannot annihilate the soul without a reason for priority, which is absent.

Checkpoint
According to the second proof, what are the two possible causes for the soul's annihilation?
A) Existence or non-existence of something the soul needs
B) The soul's essence or attributes
C) The body's corruption or the soul's weakness
D) The soul's opposition to matter or form

Key Takeaway
The second proof for the soul's incorruptibility uses a division of possibilities and shows the first leads to an untenable claim of priority due to mutual opposition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe your soul is incorruptible and cannot be annihilated, how does that change your view of the pressures and fears of this life? What specific fear in your life right now loses its power because your soul cannot be destroyed?
?
The proof argues that the soul cannot be annihilated by any external opposite. What 'opposite' in your own life—a habit, a person, a situation—do you fear might destroy your inner self? How does this proof challenge that fear?
?
If the soul's persistence is as certain as the mutual opposition argument suggests, what accountability are you avoiding today that you know will meet you after death? Give one concrete action you will take this week to prepare.

Refuting the Objection that the Soul's Attributes Depend on the Body
The author refutes the objection that the soul's attributes are conditional on the body using circularity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the soul's attributes (life, knowledge, power) must be intrinsic and cannot be conditional on the body, due to circularity.

Core Idea
The soul's attributes are intrinsic, not derived from the body – otherwise circularity.

The objection argues that perhaps the soul's attributes are given by the body. The author answers by showing that the soul's attachment to the body itself requires the soul to already possess those attributes. If attributes were conditional on attachment, then each would depend on the other, which is logically impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the objection carefully: the opponent suggests that the transient form (at death) could be a condition for the soul to have life, knowledge, and power.
Notice the phrase 'transient form' refers to something that leaves the body at death.
2
Analyze the answer's two premises
The author states two premises: (1) The soul's attachment to the body is conditional on the soul already being living, knowing, and powerful. (2) If the attributes were conditional on attachment, then each would depend on the other. Understand each premise before moving on.
These premises are the core of the argument.
3
Understand the circularity argument
The author concludes that allowing attributes to depend on the body creates a vicious circle (دور), which is logically invalid. See how the premises lead to this conclusion.
Circularity makes the position impossible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما السؤال الرابع : وهو قوله : « لم لا يجوز أن تكون الصورة الزائلة عند موت البدن ، شرطاً لكون ذلك الجوهر القائم بالنفس موصوفاً بالحياة والعلم والقدرة ؟ ، فجوابه : إن كون النفس موصوفة بالحياة والعلم والقدرة ، لا يجوز أن يكون شرطاً لتعلقها بالبدن . وذلك لأن تعلقها مشروط بكونها في ذاتها حية عالمة قادرة . فلو كان انصافها بهذه الصفات ، مشروط بتعلق النفس بالبدن ، لزم افتقار كل واحد منهما إلى الآخر وذلك دور . وهو باطل . فهذا تمام الكلام في تقرير هذا الدليل [ والله أعلم ]
And as for the fourth question, which is his statement: 'Why is it not permissible that the transient form at the death of the body is a condition for that substance subsisting by the soul to be described by life, knowledge, and power?' So its answer: Indeed, the soul being described by life, knowledge, and power cannot be a condition for its attachment to the body. That is because its attachment is conditional upon it being in its essence living, knowing, and powerful. So if its being characterized with these attributes were conditional upon the soul's attachment to the body, then each of the two would depend on the other, and that would be a circle (دور), and it is false. This completes the discussion in establishing this proof, and God knows best.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objector suggests that perhaps the soul's attributes of life, knowledge, and power are conditional on the body: the 'transient form' (الصورة الزائلة) that leaves the body at death could be a condition for the soul's substance to have those attributes. The author answers that the soul's attachment to the body itself is conditional on the soul already possessing these attributes in its essence. If the attributes were instead conditional on the soul's attachment to the body, then each would depend on the other: the soul would need the body to have its attributes, and the body would need the soul's attributes to be attached. This creates a circular dependency (دور), which is logically invalid. The conclusion is that the soul's attributes are intrinsic, not dependent on the body.

Key Terms
النفس الناطقة (rational soul)
الحياة (life)
العلم (knowledge)
القدرة (power)
دور (circularity)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the soul's attributes (life, knowledge, power) are given by or dependent on the body.
Correction: The author shows that this leads to a vicious circle because the soul's attachment to the body already requires these attributes, so they cannot be conditional on the body.

Checkpoint
Why does the author consider it invalid that the soul's attributes are conditional on its attachment to the body?
A) Because the soul's attributes are accidents that cannot exist independently.
B) Because it would lead to a circular dependency (دور) between the soul and the body.
C) Because the body is more powerful than the soul.
D) Because the soul's attributes are only apparent, not real.

Key Takeaway
The soul's attributes (life, knowledge, power) are intrinsic to the soul, not dependent on the body, because otherwise a logical circle would arise.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the soul's life, knowledge, and power are intrinsic, then your identity does not dissolve with your body. Are you living as though your essence is immortal, or do you act as though death ends everything? This lesson demands you choose—will you invest in the soul's attributes that outlast the body?
?
The circularity argument shows that you cannot base your soul's worth on physical conditions. In what areas of your life have you allowed your body's state (health, age, appearance) to define your spiritual vitality? Will you today reject that lie and remember that your soul is truly alive, knowing, and powerful in itself?
?
If the soul's attributes are intrinsic, then you are accountable for cultivating knowledge and power regardless of your physical circumstances. What specific action will you take this week to strengthen your soul's knowledge or power, independent of your body's comfort or ability? Do not let this pass without a concrete commitment.
